Twitter Exchange

 

In Ad Age, Tim Peterson reports Twitter's rumored ad exchange may be imminent. Anonymous sources tell him that "the micro-blogging platform is planning to erect an exchange similar to FBX that would let brands retarget people who visit their sites with ads on Twitter." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012jfZgUIt_5ct7WbVlQlt31iU6Q61MsWCXOJ9bgsn80UcAGdNi2K5OXby6mAug1QZ0jEvDSoH7NK97bvIAk5DOvfozjATnC2wqs_svB2WJHm6AFlGoaiUyz7xK_KXu_tblbmso7_KsLC9SQ_yU3xwO1UyMh6Sq-V8ClWDzDre3ox5FRHLO7lo0hXBsBw_82qw-5agN_ITU5S_aFOnBuLBcSUO7XhJ3fu7>  If true in regards to Twitter programmatic efforts <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012jfZgUIt_5cS8ladCmgubjwZfo4xxROq_yHeoSrjZa8m5Rrx99pJ4R7WuOl3Oxhb6HUhaSxIkizU1OeORTu3XL1hJZEuHTtYYrWcryc4Mb1cjdODOEniUUFEubtjBSjdkGcrIIBplebKJMcUvGKXe3ndQURk41z1r7z6JR9m0CN5lcj-v99kdmWxGf61Yyj0> ,it will be interesting to see how inventory is delivered at-scale. Twitter's stream seems more restrictive to ads than Facebook's, too.

 

More Native Ads

 

The New York Times and Hearst are the latest publishers to announce plans for native advertising, according to a Poynter article. The NY Times will be using native ads in one of its apps rather than embedding them in its editorial content. Hearst, on the other hand, will be integrating advertising content into their editorial on the web and in mobile. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012jfZgUIt_5c3Y_KvDT3wH8-FQ8efxtyJ3fsHnIgjYvaJdZk6plFYwvtuqoyvCtz6pXfQ9e2Ndjopzvkv_3sx2F7xAA1WHhblYdMcDi10NQeIVnxassEz54eHbtp08Ur07BXdk_gxbus-IPlkZ3fpwhzyw9x8bFyIjv5FIJdnv_deTqrilVvgGB7iH8pSd1IaYti_Fx4CfSXHcYU6IHTm4JlM1ne8oD6odJb6G7blpI4dUbndUlgjCui0AZtl39RJ> .

 

Real-Time Gauntlet

 

Google recently announced <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012jfZgUIt_5fj6akRSj4HiJlalbIbFizQGeFMs2d2VHcn-_DPNIQS4PvtT73lHwlEjC0EKJCdG7uN6BhrowqpdjC6akhNEDqHwzQFdiSspA6Y_PK_-rO3_INBGjp4mrhnOfMVaHYxuTottNeCohq8POzge505AURzhK9nf0MoNW3bG8JcbCtoQrIr718Uh_I2lrGx5VuHDHus_irIHdtpeQ==>  access to "Open Bidder <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012jfZgUIt_5eRASb9NQDCbPfJx4gEAfe5FIPAa5ITa_7rEUmFs71d4zX_aA3hqDRwONTzxq63jBxr9iIhx2U6IN8lXqfVQmKu8QsY7XkARQn2-bKOSKzNtEtAhC2l7iKQCUVJA_YvczBY6Kb8B-4FsEHVIpu8pedJRZHcQN6RpPc=> ," technology which allows ad exchange buyers to create their own bidder in real-time bidding (RTB) environments. During Wednesdy's Q&A in MediaPost, Google DoubleClick's Scott Spencer said, "Mostly we see Open Bidder helping developers who have a great idea for an advertising algorithm get started." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012jfZgUIt_5dqaES3ed87nGAMST2OsmNpbucUGZzRg3bjQZEsokEGsse8al2v43l9HbYUvNb6oUncg2g4yrAH3lZMMYGhsHxsA6n6P6GZp8aq7v6oxis7nVuyPdutynnl3pC9Ft5qxiiNfhf6pbvcOqcQrZfCtxLHTkuXTTpfW6GEXsHBOG7avRAnyeu7znkb0MZTmR7cmGNI6SJX6QUvHCkzCPGRcOg88sLJNvgeEMc=>  This could be seen as a gauntlet thrown in the direction of AppNexus, who has successfully allowed ad tech developers to create apps on its platform.

 

FBX Skipping Brands?

 

Facebook streamed a video presentation and Q&A on practical aspects of its exchange. Watch it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012jfZgUIt_5euuUItuekpBVRLCxZj4Ms-oNXKoL8u-OU06AysFL5zi1mBD02KIXiSOKNiJy_s0egeqdN41g1mBmEbipzvy_4SIEoED90BIwZMvT5ZxjXYtDi39bHfTz3a4KuRHgqn50EVzdS4-uzTEf3_Hf1D_BiHLyGNBhKi4E8=>  Responding to a question on mobile availability, product marketing guy Scott Shapiro said, "The reason we're not including mobile News Feed is virtually all conversion objectives [in FBX] are desktop focused. We're focused on enabling success there." Shapiro had a similar answer on video- and photo-based ads: "For now the focus is driving conversion goals outside of Facebook."

 

The Momentum Release

 

Data platform eXelate takes its turn with the momentum press release, saying that company momentum includes a doubling of headcount and revenue in the past 12 months - but no specific numbers on either. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012jfZgUIt_5dlhPDOx8c5xcL266hWfmBCc_O5lQNkatNoWtNxfYTrs8Ia7dL3DU7NoTCbE27D2wQlNCBeSEMD7cqkh8bLQeg4dq0OqR3P44209raGgeH9soSXx2mNtTgNlghVaD1JEiV6U6TSDhBmai6SLtwjQh7PV60MZnjfIaHEYqqEjET0g0cdKie5QSyJDoYqL02R7K4M_VV17bERQA5V1hL4tkbP222z8DD1lTdgUPR2CqKl-3SP50-pz90JRl4Gk4ec390H3ZpohhWP_7xBmUm3HGFYiZ4-hwJPBS6Hz0xMEv8n5Q==> . In an email, a company spokesperson says that revenues have reached "double-digit millions" and headcount will hit 100 this summer.

Login With Amazon

 

That's the name of the product - Login With Amazon. Clever, but Amazon wants to find a way to compete with the Google and Facebook logins, so like many of its infrastructure pieces, it's making available "The Login." See the promo site <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012jfZgUIt_5fbmE2YLR8Z9tO3rrzqnO3M6G4XXQj7-miqvwC-1rKD-vD9D1lCrZSx5TAr7rpjV0_XdExCLRTmIBNBXaaV7fFkyyN4qvQJ8st_cNHzQdIH-A==> . The site proposes one (among several) benefits to publishing developers: "You can spend less time building a user management system and more time building your product." Marketing Land notes <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012jfZgUIt_5dY5sBekPrgzN5RG8W42J2eNMT43lUfDh-z2yntX1C7O2HDYgr_ilcmnpniY51Wt4vJT5ts5CZMqbLDGNtTXSMTD-oKijkkzWekpOY-bTJNk6UJb0yfFFO5a_nmWxqvyPCIv5kR40ZJRQaECojlstBFyHCI-hlxYa4li6OBigqEexjjd7ZY_H5jk6J2LkQ34gQnXf3Jy6wT46eAK-nxjqmlWkEJazWkLiU=>  the "hooks" into payment systems - very valuable data, obviously. Also, this could provide addressable advertising opps down the road.

 

Displaying Email

 

First-party ad server and analytics company TruEffect, led by DataLogix's former COO Finn Faldi, announced a biz dev partnership with email service provider Yesmail Interactive that will bring display ad retargeting to Yesmail's clients, courtesy of its email data. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012jfZgUIt_5eUpvuqyjaC7FASAhfzqNUZ_9GZSk81z0pyI_BWc2fAH_G9DA4NLoslN8gFL6-W2qbsiRj2-vxsU9w4nV8slwbORN9xWmEDHNAwFHxgJlLo_-FNordfOcS9eaGFGWPxc_SO8xa_44JjpIASkC0JBRkTXENXvOWRXnyNoh1OL0naSchxVxZAaA4jJe4-V9NUrerWN6IUBzEYrNfcIkVrSzLnxoNCWKoIWvWSRopaX9tJqji6anRvpYUP8zuq4m5tCxghToN3DhcS2GkJifB8AqwKqfoNNrWTnSLb0Umi3X7_bg6LyhfF6OX62xSfmrIMP0LDGSbz6uxrRBRoyV83Ue3lEWcOTZbLlXsm90_LDib7lZix7hGNPCwb> . Everyone loves email addresses, as they provide a potential match from online to offline databases. Addressability, here we come.

Meeker's Ad Spend Trends

 

Mary Meeker, formerly a Morgan Stanley analyst and now at VC firm Kleiner Perkins, released her latest "Internet Trends" snapshot of the online ecosystem at the All Things D D11 conference. Given time spent on the Internet, whether through mobile- or PC-based devices, Meeker sees a $20 billion ad spend growth opportunity ahead in the US alone. See the 117-slide report on Slideshare <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mAJF4XqZQv2seaFV9VBXsPVqU1Z0md-id8sNYxgpBobTKRp0HifVQMR-cDUhDxjkObYUs_KnI1-UBX9_96eoZanPtlKWVcmgOooQo2pQ3_2BWkFcWSUYUxqAC39_zu5fslmAdbhsnQMo1isqG5kLXwxZJVOMv2Vox8IBLMKvFgSzkRqsY98edw==> . Also at D11: Apple's "sole motivation" for getting into mobile advertising? CEO Tim Cook says it was about developers, developers, developers. Watch the full interview here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mAJF4XqZQv3rTvULNhOWMVUpoeGf_nI1VuyRSsHR9BSm6a2rZtsBdJxlyoOA0qzMfqV0U88hPU3TlYP8CFkezc1USwVBYmgD6d3_v3KqdNRFu_8slgzYig4DrHbnk5gNslaL6ZJ0cPLXQSMYmddCiXzUhrlnsE744dCR-WGwypKstov3ecmFR-8_B0RhfoQu> .

 

Engaging Metrics

 

Pounding out the engagement metrics drumbeat, Googler Becky Chappell reveals findings from her company's display ad benchmarking tool in a DoubleClick Advertiser blog post. She says, "Since the summer of 2012: The frequency with which people interact with an ad when they see it on the page has grown ~60%; The time that people spend interacting with an ad has grown ~21%. People are spending on average 10 seconds of time interacting with an ad..." And more... Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mAJF4XqZQv2S9l-0Y4PMvI7rJZQAGin2PAziqfi23Mpr8Kt8cQ-kDnGKVDAq6DP6709iKH77OxZh5Jb4J2uAaaf0d0WasyppQtT6kHEOoCSYWPaCZh2KiZ9B_bl93Z570np-PDxKiJL6GBQUjcGI-El5uetsJbB0xj0l_1TCfkLKhQuNbWivI4MHYU_v23v-MyqY7rXp6fXQHbD_uQrbIw==> 

 

Facebook's Brand Safety Woes

 

Some big advertisers have pulled ads from Facebook after they appeared next to offensive content on the site. Although Facebook is working to remove any of the reported pages, it's not an issue that will go away anytime soon. "The backlash 'feels like a watershed moment for Facebook,' said Christian Purser, head of digital at ad agency M&C Saatchi. 'They do have to take responsibility for content if they are to continue growing their advertising.'" Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mAJF4XqZQv2kDvK1VQTBLEIZpI7rbJDvHY99HMKbc7K_GphRQNlG73iwfiApajzIQ75LFW8-zLIjOf7Ts9ZmauIaUMvPuJdyNJIJN-W4d47NFNB6vpKWOdy4qMEBRBKMkhWIqQ_J7v8aATxxcp8DG-O-VaEmW4DeivMeGZQneWfc39ladu5Xj6ILUDVyLW4HZheTPdVrRW57Sus-3jEPig==> .

 

Funny Facebook

 

Facebook may attempt product placement on a VH1 show to promote the Facebook Home app, ValleyWag is reporting. An email and some drafts of the sketch were leaked to the publication from Viacom, but no official sources are given. Although paid product placements are nothing new in television, this would a first for Facebook. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mAJF4XqZQv3aR0FwjcgwazOr-FdYIYvcnzRkAQ8M6sjUwPMOCyg9GO4aY5f_DdC0K-pgZ0lyGKXi95ngpFD2CNbAbnRpPcgliSzCA46Nbgqjq9f-xJcujF72iWmZPBwwaYdA_JNQsYBGRq0jdxfAqQViFwpIaWzTLqMUxUrn3UhNwQsPZvDJSU1lV6BqxysSDjWxfqbzhA24asWcFJz1RQ==> .

 

Online Video's Ascension

 

Cisco released a report showing that online video will be more popular than Facebook and Twitter in just four years. According their findings, the amount of online video users will double from one billion in 2012 to two billion in 2017, and online will account for 69% of consumer internet traffic. Gigaom reported on the study here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mAJF4XqZQv29iwZ5wqJLW_KZ-rTGVL0t_awKva06rAKPt3_7iXSOy125ezKCw0o38UGyH-iptcBm0etEPss5z3IARuNIIXed_Qr1GX03rlrLlVfjKWvib3ZAxiTN5jDwphjelWp22U4wyDUcJ3JW-RiDM8aUYNG_IgYfQt6LKYeQC0lN_D-L315PkgqXzPTUhqxE_whY8ALOuiR8ESrgNx4X5L8jvXwz> . They fail to mention, however, how much online video traffic will actually be driven by Facebook and Twitter.

Retargeting Semantics

 

Advertising jargon is constantly evolving, but understanding key terms can help marketers make better decisions. Lionel White, VP of Technology Operations at Magnetic, gives an overview of exactly what retargeting means in a Search Engine Land column. He breaks it out into two parts: site retargeting (bottom of the funnel), and search and social retargeting (mid-to-top of the funnel). By recognizing which one a marketer is using, different data and metrics should be used. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mAJF4XqZQv0qnvgrK7RydJDgzvwH0FwfxAdEv5W-OZ5dem14Yg5bR77v1Y2ekjhdJ3_eWgOhFg8z6DCA9QDCEWitkG30gwjRKIjwBHOmGuy9Zj5iSwRB1g1f4pTNEYtm3dJujOyH0cg6m9Pm0ClA1gwy2FmIRTN4> .

 

Death Of The Banner, Part 4369

 

Startup TripleLift claims it seeks to create a viable alternative to the banner ad. Its "native ads" platform takes popular photos from social sites such as Pinterest and turns them into ads that work on both desktop and mobile. "We're living in a world where cookies are probably not going to be around, and banners are being ignored," said Ari Lewine, co-founder of TripleLift on Adweek. "Plus, we're more mobile more than ever, and the Internet is increasingly visual." Twitter CRM Matching

 

AdExchanger's Twitter ad strategy prognostications <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lR1JcxPH2Ydf7Dvqt39cPzJSPz1BPpw0FBc6WDeUbTdNESR7i-h0JCw5p3OIkI3Yy0oOq2l0Nii6TGT0ICdE-fhXzFmyh1CQYLPtO3YNRhOvJkpRrU_nEw_IvKUPgkUKUVaVNLOOGB2qT0YcYiM2PrizSoYZugUlv4LDinzTEWWmZoQt4HRs1BQCpGh3Z-G5>  may be true. Twitter is rumored to be releasing a customer matching tool similar to Facebook's Custom Audiences product, which will allow advertisers to target their customers on the site. Although there is no official word from Twitter, Bloomberg "sources" expect the feature by year's end. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lR1JcxPH2Yejocj_exgThqIFuwm6TUqu1EhdYIc2cswFExwQvimXyx9k995tvSS-qdl_YsimCkThkKIurQPqNlFl6wc3RbquKdbF-JRo8kT3Yi0gPsCXyx0E9ZHq4s1l9uv4ClXDBDB2V7p_7s9FdnOA4qpyBB8nvEYM_m1mVvA0YSMwKuOn_IeyAlFRGOwiRRBIuJkti6128I73esib0G0La3-huGsu> .

 

Google Antitrust, EU Version

 

Google is still battling legal trouble in the EU as Competition Commissioner Joaquin Almunia says the search giant needs to improve its proposals around competitive fairness. Reuters reports that more than a dozen companies in the region, including Microsoft, say Google's offers to label its products and let advertisers more easily migrate to other platforms are inadequate. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lR1JcxPH2YfaJ6ejrStHeAmOm6Lqb1x4OwLNq2CxQE6YBFG0dRyXI4E8dNtnjKs7JmfozaIv92VYU58DDQgZGZTjAamvTseWgxH-bNRoYAviCBHzaIlnYz5AS0hHiwnkbuzitWnUwkqsnQkFcG0ZPlnIdLwQRG6t5Bdt6k3-Pe53kX_7t6vrcGecLQd77xTa1RNbVMC7ThM=> . The EU challenge follows last week's reports <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lR1JcxPH2YcmzjHO_R8oKiUm5xde051q5m_Eba_K0fmZ7PXJE6stotcsi97OKEajI0KsrSQQSO5FfG6gsft-oZdAdBCgoopy40LfXnl49I-a91lnZOW7dy9djORvmqeuq3-cpW_Pa37GVt_Cw-cFK0Coqnzy6loa1E5lH8czyRZLYDmaAjVGt5aFMYofV-LGmJfKYeRlmTnxbzwbeY8Bd69_0NO-4Vgsw8-gjEjFRN8=>  that the US Federal Trade Commission is mounting a new antitrust investigation of Google's dominance in display advertising.

 

Ads Unattributed

 

An eMarketer report aggregates available research on adoption of multi-channel attribution tools. The upshot: everyone agrees the stuff is important, but it's still early days. Only 26% of companies are using advanced attribution, but 28% say it's a goal for this year: "Email and paid search are some of the easiest channels to include in attribution programs. But there are still a number of digital and offline channels that businesses are hardly tracking, such as TV, mobile and print media, according to the Econsultancy and Adobe survey." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lR1JcxPH2YdOYbJGXEz6u4WFYQCDJbiZ7o-NldhTbUHbCW9rzOvndF552yO-vLCuGlGwexUTHRPYDKT_cFtEwompbdaRntsvGnh2zBA5IPeo_-rUZxJE5RbtzQJt-G9haM6pSSEUGFAOZ2KhV_8MV9mRcwYDy_eE0pF-f57nUtCNqmlw4eM-n5nKhBFIqT_gHvdRj5bBqClxeZaVYw8u0rF1JWVXoi3EdVwPPCzlceI=> .

 

Tablets Eclipse PCs

 

IDC gazes into the crystal ball and sees a prolonged PC doldrum, brought about in part by rising demand for tablets. The researcher "now predicts tablet shipments will exceed those of portable PCs this year, as the slumping PC market is expected to see negative growth for the second consecutive year." Of course, fewer desktop machines means fewer desktop ads, which will shift the bulk of display formats to smartphones and tablets. Press release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lR1JcxPH2YdBDxWLJZkkAS0otkmRlvKkE2VmjKUT-4ihB7KIdBqNmy3PO0G_gsNV_9P_-vCOnKKxitZ49bM0WjXS8XiGDQeo_xA_5hV3G7IE-RkhGkppo1yIZOCAftpPW5LvqqYaFDWsryB3mkfCafluVJoyaO_tVnbae7pSQDg=>

Yahoo & Video Ads

 

At All Things D, Kara Swisher taps her Yahoo sources and finds that the company is hot on the trail of Hulu with a $600-$800 million bid for the video site. This syncs with previous rumors reported by Bloomberg <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wt4kgg9T278wTp3yLlsf7S-zSAsxdaTnuMsWo67X7WVRmK8hZTUyHMWF5Ff6BBYFc1bu6SHepGQXp9tL_oKZzSGTZJTbeufS04jIQZ0tbdzL4HDudflTVkRTmylfuE3hD4sqN1Z6ZvBz31cm0Hv0QMMpOaPdnVM2lMCUZhVYCtxOCyXinXKJiX_ExU3FmsrnHcQH6Clw0taVlpOEWbvOJwmNKCr1l1VGYZ6_BDFXi6Y=> . Swisher paraphrases sources who say "...while allowing the bid to proceed, [Yahoo CEO Marissa] Mayer is more focused on the integration of Tumblr, as well as other acquisitions that will bolster other key product areas." Corp dev is driving this one. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wt4kgg9T27_kN-KueN86_vC1mIBjUviqVc5weysbmBqcZOfJWXcWMuZ4zbLGthLKQcdQalFRgVgwJQIuIR3PQ4Mjx3V6tJoNQYjsMZyLKkzW2C7zEz1voRTODzJItXsty7mWV8EANoA3jQhlSpDbT5WcH01C_XXjblwgoivJqLVRV50LqVIBpNVH7r83pdNdppBUoKZ2paMOPRfNeNUGnVmPhsRDmhLeFCXK5gFmT7gwhqS5ikRemtpxbKNaHSMczjRYeNtNwPVuM5AMvdaqKQ==>  Yahoo is looking to create a better video story for advertisers. It recently lost out on a stake <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wt4kgg9T27-oExZj_GPvqb0VqGVUfiCz8FbcxjQxWaOSnjPhi6c2jYTbgk58debMH5ULLpI4rI42hggJyYZY-Whr98wrGh6i6EOBuIygVd4GQJSIydiSPcwB4LoohuLPIw2ejRch3MhO3Vwm6TlB_v4YHksmjc6YtgIFc6_eENA=>  in France-based video clip destination Dailymotion.

 

AppNexus IPO Update

 

In a feature in the NY Post on New York City tech companies aspiring to a $1 billion+ Tumblr-like sale, AppNexus CEO Brian O'Kelley shoots down any thought of an imminent AppNexus IPO. But, O'Kelley adds coyly, "The investors would be disappointed if we weren't a multibillion-dollar exit for them." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wt4kgg9T27_hrhmtJuGZKoMZIZN7x1YlA78_uXcVDSH-NjJbWhrkj3pYMQh8bx40ZsHvt1sC2P6WOgZui46FMjP_KAUxWOzfq1TkrefMmV5cSQYJEI5W18ozevYC-PigoTTPhVodTKBE5g-gB0vDLJ_WMIRxgDp07-3wkPCqX6aT-HbEYLHp4JlHGoN1N_Qyi_sTqDtXhRE=> .

 

Programmatic Catch Up

 

Programmatic buying has gained a lot of traction, but in order for growth to continue the supply-side needs to catch up. In MediaPost, Adrian Tompsett outlines six areas SSPs can improve, including transparency, improved impression quality and eliminating fraudulent traffic. "The efforts of many suppliers who have proactively improved the quality and transparency of their supply are to be lauded; however, these limited efforts are not sufficient to continue to guide the market towards programmatic nirvana." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wt4kgg9T279A8XrdZir5486XaVUtBuiK5PY8n7evwkS3ieUrbzg9o4vLz5uIiIyJJGa2A90ktC4wtLljDJPbG-kPQL9G3sUy4r63p9CHDNsg3T7vg8pPAdHFJLl84NGHM8P2JdQV3TffhDW5D3Fxb7ChZHFeMho4gFI6WRwLelaDmdiXl5eotQssXQHzeKfNMOMGtlNgQ845zV12i3t9HNs2aQ2eIwxPQIt9n30qiDDdIp8ddst18oERqtaEp8qe> .

 

Same Circulars, Different Format

 

Newspaper circulars aren't going away, they're going digital. NSA, a division of Orion Holdings, is allying with Wishabi to distribute e-circulars to over 200 million newspaper subscribers. The technology allows for more personalized circulars as well, with targeting at the behavior and interest level reports Adweek. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wt4kgg9T278sbeMhWWSLwF_09rvKzkjyymMH1lsTZNK1gNgqU48ftcgxRQKlI7qHpz71Hew0-fCOANa7OUWR9YCyT90qjzreRnB-SmFMDqfND4C8MWqmIidZM5cMZxKVCOF6I-sC_t1jEW9G0nuTmQCcD5pIetHUHuGrY4NmnQFhgTuFYfJPb7_zcf8j0d8gayVc6nMPhfFYWNRB-WsjGA==> .

 

Google's Emerging Markets

 

Google is hatching plans to install wifi networks in bandwidth-constrained regions around the world, reports The Wall Street Journal. One theory goes that these networks would be rolled out in coordination with low-cost smartphones running on Android. The upshot could be billions of new mobilized Google device users plugged into the company's products. Messaging, search, maps... and ads! Read it.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wt4kgg9T279K5eZm2kalr0xJZI4WAplT_9NYZzOf5QP2hY_9NsobhwwSEg2oI6x24xJ3EjtbftQIMLrKMbTbZ6LQ4u3NeGCbLngZYORF-IVsgSI89AdMrzm3OqBcOs5SQI_PnL9CtmFZLjP7K_3hqrxMivuy4c4jVEtTuGW34MKB4wsFJq4Kynh_hiPf3--zKUSMY_dGB0EDw3pJazaQa9r6FZbPsjjkfNLm_RZitvQ=> Meanwhile, read about Google's "really big data" plans in TV according to ReadWriteWeb. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wt4kgg9T279xU-NuqF5dYhQgKwcPi1bTIYEuKzD4bI0g9DRsciqBarqL4rGSBvGsdc-XqB8wtDUR4_KOCLpZBDnDlwNlm2oxVo07KKqlB6IsDZ49jzOYFMJ7RIUHyZUAs86v-foZeTDrGPQljex2e78TIlHuXxLGml-J3IM8F5tbkXn8LVlCbJ4tETM8z3Sm2U3J3j3nnrvsfNyvn5nk8JK6nH33sRl7>

Data Bank

 

As big data gets bigger, more companies are turning to DMPs to help manage all that collected information. Most companies don't have the resources or time to make use of all the data they receive, so that's where DMPs step in and turn the information into useable statistics for targeting and measurement. "By looking at your audience and how they're interacting with a particular ad or promotion, you can take those learnings and feed them into your current efforts and your next campaign," said Mark Zagorski, CEO of data provider eXelate. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wt4kgg9T27_iiO59UzRPmAZSuTl-v7u_FxO5CkY6AA3eVLp8mrwt3kQOQvTf5U_adJxyGZsQSWWKvC2VsdzqKH9PU29EiAg92MKDlkJTKU7RtJKG9DfqLFSgjdmja47QKzhBOjGNvv0bWKIljfyYPY2UHtrfR0ZC_3aoC15eqr_LWoZ9JuiLbmZLs1fTdHNYVGglrALFiLY=> .

FTC Probes Google Display Biz

 

The Federal Trade Commission is prepping a new antitrust probe into Google's display ad dominance, just four months after ending its last investigation of the company (which found no wrongdoing). Bloomberg sources say, "FTC investigators are examining whether Google is using its position in U.S. display ads...to push companies to use more of its other services." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KXob7hB3-mW8U7lt8U0oUswcUT473o3UU-7gkU9eL3tBXSSzJattCgH8JvE90i8fcgTZ_4GzDIv6sJ5XVXlrHWnplCUIim-rHjUqpp0azU1ZuqlgFQycZagh0hsvCANQRGHLDZuSwtDr1KyY7lyY4UMk7LU9mKs3QL9UT-R9MVhyG7DKctJTo_sPl7xTVnTu8QPluxyLspDwUD8tmaWnKLSqONzbJnDqoP7WN7Fodzw=>  It's been six years since the FTC approved Google's DoubleClick merger, calling the display space "dynamic."

 

Tremor IPO


 Let the games begin. At long last, one of the promising online video advertising technology company has filed its S-1 registration statement in preparation for an Initial Public Offering (IPO). What's it mean? "Convergence" of TV and online may finally be happening. What else? We get to see all of Tremor's financials such as, "From 2011 to 2012, our revenue increased from $90.3 million to $105.2 million. This included an increase in revenue derived from the delivery of in-stream video advertising from $75.5 million to $99.7 million, or 32.1%. Additionally, over this period, our gross margin improved from 35.2% to 41.7%, driven in part by the adoption of our performance-based pricing models (...)." Read the S-1 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KXob7hB3-mU4rQB_f6ZUhQsGJjfnevu3HyqjNRH-RP_FCStQTv9WpKe4u7FrO-b6LhbN1KjVRRh3OT-UfEPYNAwoMsU5B2F8DgJtYLf91MB9JI3ADjswqFihyqgL1WxVhEb_i0Nox9Muw93ygIQPHeM05CpDBpqTiuR0Pl8-Lz2bPYe20yPvZDxBJDrGUOuIsrGgwTRARXk=> . 

 

Simulcasting Twitter Ads

 

Working with TV networks, Twitter is letting advertisers sync up their TV and Twitter campaigns. A blog post says, "TV ad targeting works by using video fingerprinting technology to automatically detect when and where a brand's commercials are running on TV." Then, when a spot airs, Twitter can serve a Promoted Tweet ad to users who've previously tweeted about the show -- lending a magic-seeming (or creepy, depending on your POV) synchronicity to the ad message. Considering this together with Twitter's new "Lead Generation Cards <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KXob7hB3-mVm7v8wOf62gsAWCLEmHv4H1AEVH7eK83CQauwPvZpEFoFZ_PW50iQgWvkmQxmSw2_isdBBFqQZsxwkCTwOEIJdbLtSB_Jgd_6qZL2451ZwKs2qrvuise5Afjy7Xvw8mQwXfeLlFzOuEg1rHF98plrtqY2dRWr_FDWBPkLv3iTg3w==> ," it seems the blue bird is getting more real-time and data-driven with its ads. Read the blog post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KXob7hB3-mWsZKqbpiaoPnYLl916hbqeaudexLQpDGYZrYrkcSn7AVIyu4w6flkbCo4lnhCWEkWfuiYgWxnqjgKeSQX9_s2TfXnEORfRK7rbBireGWLbLpCjgAMyDJwVRqhBWYD90BmFZERQbagGbDELyiXqABQ9dqK6C85VwZmAWrCDRv99Af9FNEhyB-AkQaPvEz_ymMy8YZ1oQUZUvnOLSJGNQh4xvdManAChj60=> , with handy video.

 

Programmatic Music

 

RTB works well for the music industry, which is why Sony Music has partnered with a "boutique trading desk," Huddled Masses, to handle its campaigns. "Because Sony Entertainment spreads its budget around to several different campaigns aimed at very-specific audience segments, it isn't able to meet minimum investment thresholds for larger DSPs or trading desks," Charles Cantu, CEO of Huddle Masses told Mediapost. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KXob7hB3-mVdsAeNrd-twEKWpyrFh6ghDuw40it-aWEeha5dBmK5lDSRDwyX-dP1t45Hh-nNpf5kbdo-szNojPsDybiNbu88rcyOCwJ4vFcpejvaF84RARLHoPTPUYOpAjSyjvkzy7A33qUP9rRR_kcKy6fRFCeUBiimgOBDuZ7aVT_PlpjQYMG7uECMEzQsmbAshtq_XO2b9ecpCNiGF0VCxtsSnPZd5T2DFT7_V9Ji00qE1EPVsuaThurfjAo-> .

 

Latin Private Exchange

 

24/7 Media's Real Media Group is debuting a "premium marketplace" for Spain and Latin America. The WPP media shop's Latin marketplace, dubbed Acceso, will gather inventory from major publishers across Spanish-speaking countries "These regions are connected not only by a common language and culture, but increasingly through business as the number of European companies and investments grows throughout Latin America," said Larry Allen, Real Media Group's SVP. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KXob7hB3-mWXmCqUkAv4FHqclTzlaUABg3DLDBPci5HgdXbPsLKhExGOl-odhcwwrIhFvU7o9HhVS_igkF4sEGTyDIBV1RJCNhDiHV2etR4oVcoSX-4SZ6O9WoCA0E89bIT__LzQOkARYxDi_mbEDGPS9S1_KGboZoC_q8D-4Dk=> .

Programmatic Effectiveness

 

Fast Company's Francine Hardaway talks with Rodney Mayers, the CRO of Proximic, who says effectiveness has not yet caught pace with efficiency in the programmatic arena. "Efficiency is a work flow problem that can be solved by programmatic buying. But solving it will not necessarily move product unless it is combined with effectiveness--what makes people act," Hardaway writes. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KXob7hB3-mW4h4_nIrejuq8DdDEFdC4c5jDZQAMuroh4jTIFgDgHgmQ-D9aVnlwLkcjT-3xWWNUjLZ_BNwxId9qWQy2YBKa6SgcmY5XQnzgriQbOKm7Kf5SMNEvRZvjd2aUQAIKnTB4VPHJo6fVZSVWeE1sguK2o3KjDMQprWcTlzHPZG95H4P8T0uYaUMs4694BKbSGAIU=> .

 

Geo Sense Fence

 

Geo Sense, developed by Bangalore-based AdIQuity, will bring geo-fencing <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KXob7hB3-mWpdhM_xsE7uVl0IN3p2HPrCKYwUKZ-hyh-c6n81xIQltOv-v7n9biiOS7kOqDGLn0SgSfUBPJhEA1Kwz7K425OtTKTsy3ua-F_dy8jcMvhyH526CROUfg3l47o14tX7rivdXpomai5LghPIrUYeDH0XQCHK2Kr3Ew=>  to its mobile ad product. The company works with mobile ad networks, DSPs and media buyers to increase global mobile traffic. "While mobile advertising has increased manifold across the globe over the past few years, this has also created demand for more specific targeting parameters," said head of sales Rajiv Narayan. Programmatic Out-Of-Home

 

Signs on sticks - can you buy them programmatically? Xaxis thinks so. The WPP trading desk is adding out-of-home buys courtesy of sister company Spafax and its geo-based audience segments (with Vistar Media's help - Digiday <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aeXFE9nVreVIdESg67sf--eCDXWvQ9hMnziil6dbshyD2U7-iSf27B3uoTKjfmO6Mxbshqz3--GW4dYvkn8eXL_b610kmywO51eW6SczjynW4DzttuT8dVkejzHPeS13hjmJy5LnSehBmJGa0x7l2tmnRll5s5uhuN-jQUhIeGLRSF49u6ayltNzn2Z8u25E> ). The venues: "taxis, shopping malls, doctor's offices, stadiums, gas stations, office buildings and hotels." Press release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aeXFE9nVreVoAlAYLfSU5Y5Oedvy5yPXanLCvVeA-aym7CZP5c0GVXF0HLNjjPFt_FWEbh-0F_9qqWCGMXQ76ekZ5IdurBRWV6asoww1JUQHW9FPvMqO0xCWwsh3Si8BdOzvFrIOuDUBjvgZtnB7pWX6xpYln1iJhO7Lz2jV2FLDW1EzUPKmfpXXjo_c10QyctU7ESzwJhM=>  Volume is about 1.4 billion monthly impressions across 100,000 screens. At a glance, this appears to be a data enhancement more than an addressability shift. WSJ recently covered Xaxis and Spafax's moves in radio and OOH (out-of-home). Read that. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aeXFE9nVreX0SfQq4IKI17_DT9hx5_W229Vks0mfuqeHdV8iyEMhnWGp3NjVVNzVG2-oRFs4JQBzqOoSGqc5fQ0RHGPeKnSREuAl_83-WN25tUBOm9toMzS3eK9r8kvNjDd0ij7QaKtd15Iv3qH233FIuxHWao8xNkIGiyGbwJuQ9EtJKid2TdocA7jj7j38>  Meanwhile, in other OOH news, OOH buying platform AdStruc has integrated <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aeXFE9nVreWHvbTpT6E73jYNAGiUnIB0Pxp62ozDOn8Bag-sQUMV3cMg8424j0L8hiEPbHvgX5riVxQ6MVhRo-3JC1zKyf5osNWVgpgTJWbvh_U7J62L2QFFS8626y9PDOcDgEfLN22N0jVxTisw_jlSypPvQrUb1m3ctebb34dg0Ga8wcqlvwfbdXAYdRkMACQtuFLxCXLiZvFvicaxoZjP5V-Pup7j>  into agency workflow system Mediaocean.

 

Twitter Lead Gen

 

"Twitter" and "performance" aren't often mentioned in the same breath, but that could change if a new in-feed lead-capture tool takes off. Project manager Mitali Pattnaik writes in a blog post, "Users can easily and securely share their email address with a business without leaving Twitter or having to fill out a cumbersome form." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aeXFE9nVreXxsAr6dljGMkctsvcoxVQECUBu0Ig8YJsPrL4Cwv0N9PWK63fiRNr_LNmbKce7EcQs3itOy4_6lhuuQ4KxAtqxFQvZuG_ybnYu0sdNiEPEj9aW_pxTtfgvmvgoKlwF-AlRASB_pFNXoBYV-ZRn6lagci62UcfPq8NVSoyMdgReos8iNZisKrwJ_OCl57aRiNvUrxTH6tNdb5Mlf8mjR_gY>  Being tested for a few months with New Relic and Priceline and a few others, the feature is for "managed accounts" only (i.e. direct sales). Before it goes wider (API and self-serve) Twitter will need to resolve issues such as frequency capping at the user level and addressability. Another key question: will Twitter support CRM matching à la Facebook's Custom Audiences? A rep tells us, "Not a functionality we currently have."

 

Algo Marketplace

 

DataXu has created an Algorithm Marketplace to add to its programmatic marketing platform. The marketplace consists of algorithms DataXu has collected from solving various problems, and it will help make programmatic more effective. "The DX Algorithm Marketplace allows marketers to leverage Adometry's best-of-breed attribution solution and their own algorithms in a single platform. The result for marketers will be increased ROI from media buys on DataXu as part of their overall omni-channel media strategy," said Gad Alon, VP of Business Development for Adometry. Nielsen's a part of the marketplace too. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aeXFE9nVreVE82vJXxMDMAVsuAHB-g2d53JSfln7uhlgPE_xtBlF9_CEBHA7bzaJNEuDFg2PhpRxI4MPDBfRsXi_2BqpAqTi1Z7xRksgXtf3db14DArHk0aQPk_WlH2bZua5u_Ar53BUFJOb__WEUSh-0vzcjQKQbpfDmhjTdC6xx-r4PS4gZw1imc82BdXG> . And MediaPost <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aeXFE9nVreWzPzhVq3d41HSofSidK4Hhz6Ue78Nq4yDknFNCWAsQ6PUD9zT_QYyZ357ZiULW3eqt7-pzRan8mk2CvIGpI6qKsdWjWQzadvJc11PpZos868x52WDxf12Nmtm7P2DWFo2PzCnOiBx_UpObkoPqUl0bLu6eFKkyCLDTDcmzLpdVqUAuJLiAbb3L090z8DMTQoPbmgwypTGDeZrtvDv5T0kPBELLUzEJIpc=> .

News Feed Retargeting For All

 

AdRoll is opening up its Facebook news feed retargeting feature to all of its clients and will soon make it available for new customers. The self-serve tool debuted two weeks ago <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aeXFE9nVreXe36Bjm-H_ZIFT6_yTzcWIOxKlJPDhD6IvrHXG1AuWztmIrlk66hmxKIIzZKIA6-6jHfvFMOyXF5GJsmQyZHu2bXenfBZsSCMoXzP-jTVYiKskxBjpkagQN6ozWkb9rlQK-f1gZ5G_MruoNFj4EHPV>  and allows advertisers to create their own Facebook news feed ads directly from their AdRoll dashboard. "We're finding CTRs to be in the single digit percentages vs. fractions of a percent - orders of magnitude larger than standard FBX ads," said Adam Berke in the release. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aeXFE9nVreVJFVHa7fbHuFJHOE8rq44lUA-Gdyczdbq8r_KQhuvKZAyJdpHKLPDPTScv80aPl7ewK5vQwYJFAkxEFVkenQPqeHG3JFSEjbzt3eOX_d4vDmZfc9PLKf8dl3ZhbdvUJjkUrRYwICf_ZvCRJdfsIJv4> .

 

UberMedia Gets Uber Personal

 

Users of social media can expect their activity to be tracked for mobile ad targeting purposes, thanks to UberMedia. All the information the company uses is publicly available, and users must opt in to sharing location data when they open an app, but so far brands have seen increases in click-through rates, according to founder and CEO Bill Gross. "People will have to get trained, will have to get used to the fact that when they opt in to that, they're doing it for the purpose of making the ads better," Gross said. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aeXFE9nVreXlHNSTyoMztnkm_JvSzloihUm8h8xY1aZ1RaL42U3kpraD0DZdWvH5llkhUoefp4FPpkCLYP0Mac0wQQpHpelmbdYBh_GjhXJauoXKio88CG93w83oagO8TeIbtrNvd3WkQnunlgTmTpP67_TDloVkDS2EGhfdqMpI2YFJFw0Cr7OsLfKE-2jpYdcnz9e28mvzwBjie2jDpMjB9EiI4VCL>

Online Video Ads Really Work

 

Online video advertising has been making waves lately, and according to agency executives, videos work better than display ads. BrightRoll conducted a survey and found that 73% of respondents felt online video ads were more effective than traditional TV ads. Online video consumption is also on the rise, which could be part of the reason why video ads are performing so well. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aeXFE9nVreUndvBR6gUMJcux2aofb7yEQxtwsZsEenxPBE_a0uNgA0ZJA6ROMKLGs4TbjeYL8cvwywKpMZZiRF4n3WtnzTl41WiNufzbVq-ORt2g9hjsysmwjIW1mvavJvuYHQrBY24lBZBTaykKPtNOMWcrEfT2BMQq4D7KOfk1onoyvCtNix_KPlNPu8UYrCkGD4lCmYI=> .

 

Clouds Of Marketing

 

Safesforce has their marketing cloud <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aeXFE9nVreWZY0ZbAOT6CKYT_grdn1Y4m-tx_wlaUfuhtTmrw5v_w999pv2lYrcYHQaZg3gn2LNn4_cYZa31PDIOxCw45-7kp2yqOGkR0FbOrAozUwJQUaxD9eQ3Zrm1zdagXJOJ65quaGvE8VXw3w==> . Now, Responsys, whose core business has been email, is clarifying its position in the enterprise marketing space with the Interact Marketing Cloud. A release explains that the Responsys cloud "enables marketers to build a complete profile of their individual customers, design highly personalized digital interactions and orchestrate sophisticated marketing programs across the digital channels." Elementary, My Dear Watson

 

From yesterday's Smarter Commerce Global Summit in Nashville, Tennessee, supercomputer "Watson" is apparently coming to marketing in a much bigger way. An IBM release offers, "Watson will serve as an assistant in helping line of business leaders from CMOs, customer service agents and sales leaders transform the customer experience..." What's that mean, you ask? A big computer is going to help the marketer figure out the "big data" stew. A keyword to all this is improving "engagement" with consumers at-scale. Read more on GigaOm <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017OxKh4NXFJpk6zp49ke_OszinTYUFyUjoHYP-Qo09RaJ7VD9KE4FQY_44EzNSg4IIUSCg60yeb9xdpNdq2hU6NEQLSz9f-QhBePTgv14l_tV2vg9AaMtzDRaqWbP1vFDB4AmFeogdv5CSbpg5_JvDIU5zPqJiQfXKn9rhKjkMTV32tlJvFQE9_zxgGw6JnlFVkdVryEslPErrhf4oVoXpLAvItjPRG2AirmbWd9brN8=> . Will they become an acquirer in the ad tech world to pull in the paid media channel? Seems possible. In the meantime, download IBM's new 2013 marketing report <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017OxKh4NXFJq4H8NY-LchRDYTpgu2PgZ8IdyMDNy7kZRHbuHO2coDUmmWZGkNrVhXQef74yGtVDw91AbzeczVvsmL1CIrBh_blCQSTt2IbCkT9caEE17Mnn1C3RUZfqg0ze7yr6Yyulcj4QH7IdHEK4YHkhqagqE2ysLqtUXjERHN-g_kMWhblILc1Hp3SffTGAWlErHB4yMJcyefQ_GbXPlrT-hWEFlyPEno22FKhUOpYpvDEX6A8w==> .

 

Hashtag Exchange

 

Is the hashtag exchange far away? We've prognosticated previously about a hashtag-targeted exchange <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017OxKh4NXFJoqRxu4ChlmhD7UK_up7Bir0cY9ag226y5uOLpLBxCPKu3hcxp8nR9pkzMucGzThiaNY7Qt4gsreZm8Yj6WtTdVhJBUE6DVp_JQ3BYa3OE3FsvEFzMHI37BHIGoTges_N0TCs2SA16N-nn-yKPcVAcBg-sMxcPSeHKBoSN461_BSAHPG7rpnCR3>  as one extension of Twitter's programmatic strategy. Now, Inside Facebook's Brittany Darwell gets wind of hashtags on Facebook. Among the use cases, Darwell's source suggests, "users will be able to hover over a hashtag to get more information, similar to what they can do for people, apps and pages, as seen below." Better intent data in a social context, perhaps. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017OxKh4NXFJqEHWk9zgqmRmCYVuwl50pTjzF7tJ8_AHVCOWbZ0MUFfAG4ak7xUT9WN7cU3BxkV8RGSEQAFUy1XxlP2w3ucfz4HT8AvOipfcYzmcECnulL9X0hvdjAlZgtXQYGF2eL3zg=> .

 

Portals Are The New Black

 

In a think piece on Ad Age, kbs+p's Darren Herman says a "cookieless world" is imminent. And he thinks big publishers stand to benefit: "The more traffic coming to your web properties, theoretically, the more you can use big data to help optimize the advertisements and experiences for consumers. We never thought portals would be popular again, but they stand to be large beneficiaries of this evolved ecosystem." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017OxKh4NXFJrERbEgIzrjh2hW4OLznXH7mbIlUUSzAwoItrQOHgL1sdkoKdrdHL7KzqESMF2kKkter2_RGCaTTXG__p45WBnvgkq-tvieYPK4pCxTTSawxagL1u422FDTrrlA6_5P05HiHO7XQNHfKxAd6bteeUNWY8xFlN4eqhqj_u-OlgtrFYah3em7xYbCxZ8f9oq6PZKm948wozdd1w==> 

 

Going Cross-Channel

 

AT&T is going cross-platform by serving targeted ads online through mobile and on TV via its AdWorks Blueprint platform. AT&T will use anonymous data it has collected along with third-party data for the ads. Online ads are served through their Online Audience Network, and the TV ads will run through their Television Audience Network. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017OxKh4NXFJpqHm-btY-zaAtV9o3C6H_O00a4TRfvT3a5jVxsvCKgxOaALk3hOBVnMpqQRcSmAEMGxZkydSzQVWDvnKj8ByuXHg5Zmkx2YPrxZICuri-EwWSBHFN7z18MokqiLMiMQK3sQdLUrMJZ7v1_fCUi-2VWTz8miVWgvmVbqo56W_Ha1Q==> .

 

More, Better Banner Ad

 

The New York Times IdeaLab toyed around with a new way to make banner ads effective by implementing an interactive element to the ad. Wisk, the advertiser, was pleased with the results, although it didn't give any numbers. "What sets them apart is the amount of experimentation they've done," says Dan Buczaczer of VivaKi on Adweek. "A lot of the elements they're experimenting with on the editorial side are the ones brands are interested in for marketing." Welcome Ads!

 

On Digiday, Jack Marshall looks at the so-called interruptive "Welcome Ad" format that you might see when first arriving at a publisher site - as high as a $150/CPM, says Marshall. He surveys an industry voice: "'The costs are crazy, so we don't usually recommend them to clients,' [Mediassociates' Ben] Kunz added, despite his views on their efficacy. The agency sees better return on investment for many clients when buying standardized inventory or through exchanges." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017OxKh4NXFJrOL6ARFtuCwZP5E3bQbBSvSNgSl29IRQk2ltt2e76Aw51AuFVJz-Kqnyv80JtkCNpmi1NNPargXwkeK3HroCesTd1omfUoKrHWCthac0TxcIB52d3q_lp6RMQhW_tjIL7E4zq5T7T-DmJyyXb8UqAE4XI0tzwQT0ds_2H_ULUNc3sABG7R12uQ> 

 

Funding Programmatic

 

Mobile attribution company HasOffers successfully raised $9.4 million, led by Accel Partners, in its latest round of funding. HasOffers has two SaaS products: HasOffers.com and MobileAppTracking.com. "We're seeing a market shift in online advertising from the CPM or display oriented world of the past to a more programmatic, performance based approach," said Rich Wong of Accel Partners in the release. "Mobile advertisers are igniting that progression by demanding real user engagement from their advertising partners. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017OxKh4NXFJqWHGErFF4SP712dK3zVJXDMWR1MEft9-2dTvXpqHZCGQ6LqY6N9U1jrKff-JA7KsP1WloJssMC9jyF92j7nVBh2WlXbsvvQ3E-OG-iFVm5qeimh3CzUC8OXjetlLkb2YjHl7HxB99EG3oiRk-uzbEMd9aPGewMOitAoPgEoh6FyYS1XpUB3buczpthwyENTpDcGqAk4LFs32eMr29Usaq5rG3NJ0qVxQM=> .

Open Sourcing RTB

 

Google is offering its RTB technology in a roll-your-own format. Developers can access the company's customizable tool-kit for real-time bidding applications using tech from DoubleClick and Google Cloud Platform. A Google developer blog post says: "With Open Bidder buyers can significantly lower the latency of their bidders by leveraging Google Compute Engine's scale, speed, and proximity to DoubleClick Ad Exchange." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ie1IAQd0hgTVXWT50QzVqjXjxXaBPtANVebxzE5TR6tMdF5-IcXNIi-pHRY3grNzG6pkeshl8JMcmkVJqDjlWBIU6Lp2c5SNf6WmfC4yL6sFzjSARtjnHKnu3_aN3QGjvO3mqGnts9lgGWRK3D3Tclncb-4h3wNjQsWClD9ufDeBxY0_QQauDfC580Iaqq-GfbwkBMghbRgNUtQwf7w9vAiX10nStYcm> .


From Agency To Ad Tech

 

Nick Pahade, former CEO of ad tech platform TRAFFIQ and IPG's agency Initiative, is now the CEO of Poptent. The small company is a video crowdsourcing network geared to agencies and brands. "Now there is a wider industry recognition of the importance of video in earned and owned media, in addition to more traditional paid environments," said Pahade. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ie1IAQd0hgSdh4-du77lrLsagMiaZrGc0uSfrmdTL-TuPFC_zNwbSbza6p1W9CiwZJp9-07KPfnTSONi6LWCyURjOxNawtwg1fjebQEoxL7C7JH3u9zgevAWI-_4Sx75hqdNBfzqk6Q0YmEeawL_YLP-x_LBirEDpNX_Ad9N7AF9H6ZvWCksgoNAwR9dO54fwj_zGdmrQFCLXM-XnNWbe0YweYajx08i> . AdExchanger spoke to Pahade last summer. Read the interview here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ie1IAQd0hgSv6V5bVS6yBAqtQszf_AETB6hVxV4DTQxYA6de8hXuU4dQIPX6gRdSni5kZBPYp2j9yuYILT4iBKhqmMeBztIO61Z-dXBJWBXPv69YJBWYjNvMw6JAwx3GGI-ZmiU9qDqUWrRVJ-kcuDFKtWPvcwxAub-UXsQ5W3zQh4Vq0SLY8SL9f4CWSOvyPX790hlvbVh4GxQFyyZVrg==> .

Alex Frommeyer, co-founder of Beam Technologies. "In many ways, [data-tracking] is the entire point." Excuse Me Sir, Your Data Is Leaking

 

Data leakage <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ie1IAQd0hgQ31c23hcnldXajY2_lg46qE5I6nDhP9ivt_oFRxWpG-LLSZ0uBqe7hu68WZ_7Cev85WhGu5wtyP9QC5xX3WNcGrr5QEMhWFc_YTxRZ68bc27tII7mNklOFx8rCxmnbvWu5kokZEAa67B0AL6n9Cg4Iuhf_BJDgFjtouUvItXdHQQ==> , the nasty practice of audience theft by third-parties, is apparently the publisher's fault. "It's a bullshit story that it's not in their control," Simulmedia CEO Dave Morgan tells Digiday. "They have always had the power to block those cookies. They are totally culpable." There are companies, and even browser plugins such as Evidon's Ghostery, that will show a publisher all the tags on their site - although the publisher has to take a look, first. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ie1IAQd0hgSKRZVI5zNI5xdpcOQK5fPC_ElaoVhirXMJ9bSQ3OqBhfwN00uuSGJiVfphlVUFbbNzpBXCEnWVrOLTkdclaNhZ0TwE7u0SyfFkTmG1XrrCpBTuNpL3tICRFDgB_5KNSl4Gbj6uBIAvupFNczaGgXJAGWMUi4pA2pdGuKg7MTKPgJeFqEDsa1nV> .

Acquity Acquisition

 

Accenture has ventured into the ecommerce marketing space with the purchase of Acquity Group for $316 million. The move will benefit Accenture Interactive's digital marketing product aimed at CMOs. "The acquisition [complements] our strengths in strategy, analytics, scaled technology enablement and marketing operations," said Accenture's Brian Whipple. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ie1IAQd0hgTZQdIkayTNEoIRCrjpH_CgKmvmIKfgbsYvpcU-CaoFDs--y3riktMUoC2dvwkuZ_qqZh6iAi5fDAa29vWXcZvDLrNrEaDyw_VB2D59kDPyRwMC_y5w3_KAhWjnS-DzKKPA2z_GMOYAa8I_WZhHJo_3vyWRM_Lnsx57vFE-2O9m32nHDloK1DAkLm7oNRRAn4b0NPZRhc290ozGKObsaaOwm7upOoiAU6BLoDHdaFDikIZo3L29i0TLJ2xXmIdpxyxbgQNI73h3OA==> .

 

Wading Into App Waters

 

Sprint has beefed up its Pinsight Media+ mobile ad targeting product with the acquisition of Handmark and its OneLouder subsidiary. The move is all about app development, distribution and ads. "OneLouder immediately infuses Pinsight Media+ with an experienced advertising team, a sophisticated ad platform and top-rated mobile apps that serve millions of customers each day," Sprint claims in a press release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ie1IAQd0hgRpV2acA49cjscgX-BUj4I58az9V3l8ZXVZOzRKFY82M4RZaK9lugxdVHN4q1jmqiEq4plmJEgPaWWbs-Yx-l7aw0kUNaFXRVQ83nWpC-A7mQ6umPh6UTEn_dcpcZQnzq90x7fX8Xq2yGS7lxs8IY5byouGcdRXdmzS-XTFllZh6aDC6veFvOaDcXtwNpITxBvo-OkprVG3ItHUzQcrQCK4sYa9O9-E7Nr-k1jy7NpR5lYhRtLnj1M2Y_tUros5Ujg=> .

Yahoo Youth Movement?

 

Perhaps a chance to capture a younger audience, Yahoo is buying blogging platform Tumblr. The WSJ says the $1.1 billion deal is done (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qtTRKZ8FES4NvDXhb9fNAlFzLSLWcSxydV0UhpwMTltREc5speKlpa_R_3mptgN9xcKkl_jfFC0Gvix6N5VT1MmJ0lgD1AW7WcM2_mwxESAiZZSTQUcj9jq3NB0iPfZQrrLiietArB3h89VwUxYaIKjL5110CfPsFVuoz6h5CcUo-3K5xsB6f4tQTKXqypgb>  and so does The NY Times <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qtTRKZ8FES7-MhXXl3MJa3cGgcpPSqOnM06KpXri8I0pBy86ucdDuF2pRUPdRc6ZTKjODYequdFfQZtYhvVr93WKW2JvyrcsKV_FAEU4F26ZTH4mXSYVXoPfEb_l2NFGeB9ISYI7WRkno8BzFDeNThquT6teDWSNNFHFNEpaJ_fwbtZjoAuzaTj9T3_YjJ_oxMgDOaXe3m5c1zRZNTK4ZQ==> . All Things D broke the story late last week and referenced a quote by CFO Ken Goldman at [JP Morgan's Global Technology conference] as a driver of the acquisition, "One of our challenges is we have had an aging demographic. Part of it is going to be just visibility again in making ourselves cool, which we got away from for a couple of years." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qtTRKZ8FES4YotrH9C0eudIQVIq92QVrwKKrNE139qPYqwnre7V1Cb8-Eb8io0qfux_tXeBlhKrb6EOSRYjnZMwBAx3NJDMZZ4DM3-FtddJBLrYo5_vFKM87Fa0ZdN_a3IpxawXwXVt3QeAftWvIVqFm04u75YLIhO3EfpYLqIYCuepwbFbcq81LHwCVc1VyTTazfokVrV1oIIYzAeJkkokiC9Dozm0P> . A growing revenue model (advertising presumably) and management structure need to be worked out at Tumblr. Nevertheless, it's seeing consistent traffic growth. More from Forbes <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qtTRKZ8FES6hdmKTLNBGlltF0m-U4U3UN_JrDryZoAwVNS211eEppXusm5OElul_vZ8-TMUv-cH3cza0osPRXKGXcPOHTIbW4xllhOTF0RDLyzaabd4auNH4vFG0xrC6_atRc3etxib-EUjlxhxwEApPBCVC0Ip8Gpj3cQgn82lWOlSnooq283-5FvCsD3yZlq7mtigmsg0O98QVk12MpeDqNJdUDY3-rkn_f_u-GU7ItsCbeiIwBEYXsLwOlCmGFEiIy5TiyM7j7oAarYYrBg==> . A special "product" announcement is scheduled <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qtTRKZ8FES7jtML_GCT8RlXDolSea3PXwQAHYr46U5NT0RfCt4NQ-aGyAVNZB3KepMLJIT4ZSK1XNndqOTdKqCUimNE4Q45TXDXlm5jx2uOOCTqPDLkwCYD-aLJQk-yC-fuewqFiM6fMCxpjeqXKsjpDYOQxNS7oQEuUXTsUtzm08Msu0Xfm6Rc_TdTQ4F5wdYp92cHog1WXHJs7ou5AHy47D2br0ltTwIWeV9jopWRvoPytCocXWg==>  for today by Yahoo. Last but not least, Businessweek explores <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qtTRKZ8FES4sMMErMMsFK5ZwgOXZ_0qZbhlumv3CxIWcPKXB2YYZRDIDWArGwAo5VmVMIVrWBtllXqYhs56oW9f91IyjWC9U-p7UUD0SFmljFKvvTDfzE_fWHkk56TOd-oZjt3O9QgX-P97vFDS3IGZosYsYDxEHscktqzaNBuyfObsmWZST-39EUSvJ0tIsbxULFKGA9YXOUa6MrnbEokRG4F6jNHGJQQde2cY98Qg=>  Tumblr's porn "challenges."

 

Marketing Automation IPO

 

Marketing automation is on the march as Marketo raised $78 million in its successful initial public offering on Friday. The company now has a market cap <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qtTRKZ8FES51ySzwrs3XBHoHb6jpL67QRNzWFSMk9m-W9ixLRKBzkUs18UoBDTXBuYNe7ilLilv2LJVBeSzhRYohCCGhtrJaKNnRZbJB1h-Uop0YeMhkZxx8bnkYm9WqN-0Aebf6ML0Nb2RGbUyvtai3TG4JccSl>  of $857 million. This is a similar valuation to Oracle's purchase price for Eloqua <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qtTRKZ8FES7A1MJaKW7dVEl7mqzjlX629mBtdBWzF_6chUSxHsess8t-wpKWrtcKfKeX6W2PozZLRUwUsFxhwUbrGkETGowM05JUEnRrcO6tHb_eiYeNg56pmWO28XvSw-56_PB06vojfA95efoHyVo5PlTkGpaKs8FuVrzEYi0=>  last year. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qtTRKZ8FES5I0pUQlzlfGP7SHjcPQxa0ONRw4yJ0LV7c_HUhGRyHS_JF2y7pWhSN_S5-OrS5isW7mF3HhOtBVzBJ0lmAKHrlmLdcK7VkMPpymtbIheizgp569flVO6Lk8UrwdXfGcSG1Y1lzckHpMNOn2cQE835WocCncoZq3wZBLGNDR44cQL81-REqMr9OlaMYqpUlyNG7qJeBGuN9QSHHSdTlmduTfFWJAypjUIU=> . And, here's AdExchanger's Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qtTRKZ8FES79LXBfAJSfo4F6kgkCcxLDRSZ7qIPV_yP_5kz-YupXBdEAryxQdTiWjfRTjg03AclR-GGeOqobzdm6qSv0--TzHArP777ix426Ix_2YJIthnnmhiY4_nxdIiqe103O2BD_3UXwmewBzg==> &A with CEO Phil Fernandez one year ago when he said, "The market is only fractionally penetrated. Anybody that is marketing online, marketing in social and mobile environments and has any desire to build either a brand relationship needs what we do." Ad Ops Intern

 

There are apparently a lot of things a Universal Mccann ad operations intern should learn and do, in fact UM's Mitchell Weinstein outlines 17 tips to make the internship successful at his agency. Tip #16: "We do a lot of work with Google, Facebook, Hulu, Twitter, and many other really cool companies. At first this may seem fun and exciting. That probably won't last, and as you get more into your job, you might find yourself more excited about working with companies most people have never heard of (maybe the next Google?)." Read the full list here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qtTRKZ8FES5TKFCAXlZlcr6Dap9LTUbt6oTI7e4T43Ci2XK6xO2WNghnpVRJhjnHBTnBT-9BsgCnXYxvQ8s3VryNyjy6rvr5Yy2O7MZDqoKTf2vTOx5-GT8aM9v2qnlNFaQ9Yn9XJ4nUGol6M0xPvD_J7s3_ON2fk4hDd1e16eR-KyteROWnPQ==> .

 

Publicis: Not Nielsen

 

Agency holding company Publicis has told the Wall Street Journal it will go with comScore and not Nielsen for online GRP measurement. The WSJ's Suzanen Vranica writes, "The decision of the Publicis firms to go with comScore's system is significant, given the scale of the ad budgets they handle. Starcom MediaVest and Zenith spend about $32 billion annually on ads in the U.S. on behalf of companies such as Coca-Cola, Anheuser-Busch, InBev BUD and J.P. Morgan Chase. Several weeks ago, P&G, the world's largest advertiser and a Starcom MediaVest client, signed up with comScore." The client is in-charge. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qtTRKZ8FES4yAzGU-y_14oXEubOK1LnZhqtbHZc4wHWc8BJhsqAqPi3Ah7FDQP_49mOc_UAP2lXyHyRJhENVeCZHz3mh0pM7N5qg7mcjOHkUrCbN4X4C31dFgBRZLzxBDiEudA1frVxe2Dyw4TWW3iSAaL_xP7Bj8dUD8N5WMw1_a6uMjPYBMGKodtyjKwGo> 

 

Forbidden TV Island

 

Brian Wieser throws some cold water on the notion of a big happy marketplace for integrated video and TV inventory. In a note for Pivotal Research he writes, "As digital advertising becomes increasingly driven by programmatic and real-time buying, online video will increasingly be bought in this manner. But it won't necessarily follow that traditional TV will be bought either programmatically or in real-time." PDF download. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qtTRKZ8FES5GyvHoNSvGQbbBleSByAneA0HAISP_bNYD3iMarWwrhiqWHWl0yfwnvLg9f0mpgbVrsdJzv3utuxt0am6D6dYmjs_hU0OnbM3F-EHO2c1zEAC_aLrcLtNpUpq5a3kpbWz5dacnN_LoncWSvLvNCbqCY72FJgynGYiG1j59yck5VdXbsHhv6sjwHM-SRp6pjpKJ87aDtp3DtWFmLZfJEcEy>

GAN Down

 

Google is shutting down its Affiliate Network product in July, but it doesn't seem many advertisers are sad to see it go. "Affiliate marketing always seemed to be an out-of-place fit in Google's line of otherwise automated products. By its very nature, affiliate marketing relies on building relationships at a granular level with marketing partners, which requires a lot of personal attention and correspondence to achieve," said AvantLink's Chad Waite on Marketing Land. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qtTRKZ8FES4FILm6K205-uyU71Jr4HTcUJok9G2NV6hUx46DPkgednFTTSBi7biH38qjvsuiKet7uDB-oevxFFX4WqGql16-atL4j_HQESpjJNE6NXvS7tnHhYIraygmLDwuyXi1ur7pAqpz4uH2yM4zbTL4viQZSpMZmQv6CA3-izcuai2b7ny1IpKCd6wwDhWLvrF3Zgf4r3MNrnMDlhQPY9gOllKNyS6Xe9_ZQgQ0ha0IcK4Z9L-Jm4AeImJOty2JvnGoEeCq5lAthNw-kuTgkJBYUHYD6jFLJ4obVXo=> . ValueClick has been a beneficiary of the GAN shutdown with its Commission Junction unit receiving some new biz - though there's some question as to how much - a question raised during the ValueClick earnings call <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qtTRKZ8FES4gf-_GQKvKPLzBBQ8x-F5-6RZtmoCP1co1dOyQfuskm0ICbtS_Prpy_aSGO-ulnBUpb4S8K4avEp194WM_uJ7iXLO0Z7wEocbAfUgv0-gbq5lqoHMC9CpW3whXWfEyl1zjrKEA6l4MaG2PfJ32FeSDVlZ3wJdIbLY=>  two weeks ago.

 

YouTube Reach

 

In Sunday post on the YouTube blog marking the site's 8th anniversary, the YouTube blogger notes some milestones <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qtTRKZ8FES7NwdmTBOQnoChySAG0Tt8Vxq27l-dF26000PtzfKNaoQ63gVhnLzX_lV5w24m3sgOJlD_S9zKhAgSTaa_pQYpLJI9TUZzgz8y7Qx7uPXESBlKbkdcJ3phr7oUjg1rurvtMyBo1ew28FKSUzFi4245DOdSXCusuCAhhFyv8M72UrMuKOmFI0KyX> , "Today, more than 100 hours of video are uploaded to YouTube every minute. That's more than four days of video uploaded each minute! Every month, more than 1 billion people come to YouTube to access news, answer questions and have a little fun. That's almost one out of every two people on the Internet." This YouTube thing seems like it's going to be big [sic].

New AdMob

 

Google unveiled a rebuild of AdMob at its I/O conference today. The changes, which incorporate tech from AdSense, are all about optimizing conversion for advertisers and boosting yield for app developers. There are some bells and whistles here too, such as better filters for developers that want to slam the door on low-rent ads for dating sites, mortgage re-fi offers, etc. A million or so AdWords advertisers now have access to AdMob inventory. Blog post. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001pUNkJiybayQ2sqEtS2Zy3Nmok8bCG6mVRJ4lZMQjq9hVI_fB8Qk7BwMpWZZWL4KMDk1sW9J-g0O3JUVkn7OIwCALIRZWM73oIODprVvtnLi3SfgKhW3_aOiZy786qzY1vcYk_7dACt1k3zIC4eQX3ICqtWRscwWXAZbZqXZ15McIFqawRupWBxnIGAMdovZ-T_TzzGPT6Jz9rAZOSQnZXQ==> 

 

Acxi...umm

 

Acxiom is pushing hard to make enterprise data as easy to work with as Google Analytics. But it was slow-going in Q1. Earnings slides. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001pUNkJiybayR4LbuHFMd8qPUkAVVlf25_BPtqPQNPeD64xhssTGyDxUPy1jQrxFqSdwcghAguDujYL1tPcHUgCuefjwQ_tWilgSaprw1VRQDlX-FTOdgIOjfbEoul-Rok71adyWYPsJcR0aha1mNgd-EKH2WOQ06G3a5ivtUYRrmXoupCYL-D3_kXtvw1_bGYsPR-gv79Ii92jEVAT4aETdhIHbOUON988YEz83QqWCVb8LNGsfwO0_0lngybQ09rii3OY1B3ZKEsPhh7zi_J4qGQfrO8tT2JykKCUzK86RvSOiksvjOnyzlOih-5q8Fd>  BMO Capital Markets' Dan Salmon, in a research note: "Marketing and data services revenue was down 2.9%...while IT infrastructure management declined 3%...Revenue has a long way to go before it approaches management's long-term goal of double-digit organic growth." He believes we can expect divestitures such as IT outsourcing as Acxiom doubles down on the data opportunity. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001pUNkJiybayTsFPmzGCn1k_xiAwLQPbt4B9nhB1BFDCLT3vVY3Evz7WB5hHZar8A2n9kPU0pZx9Jf7c5IBbLEWq52xLKy6yRnafPDYT2EW-d63B16XtmPrdlycFB7JUHbtLQUF0BvEIrMO-DQL1i1zPVPUVQkagOqCiaaEoQCUtz8EihJe6xce9pGDpZFteES1Bh8wRE4hx3AAKnBFDw7ZQ==> 

 

Advertisers Without Borders

 

Hearst's new division, Totally Global Media, seeks to streamline advertising internationally to make the process more efficient. "Before now, if an advertiser wanted to buy across every edition of Cosmo, there was no way to do it," said Gina Garrubbo, SVP of Hearst Magazines International and now SVP of TGM. "There is a need [for this type of service] in the marketplace and a number of clients who want to buy multi-country from one source." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001pUNkJiybayRbsRIojtdsuqc0xHY7jXpbwVtKoZ0RLt09EoKI3v3uT2rBGI9fwXwjga9DiMU_tPYpQiRQWkBYc6dQ163HoWaB3a_LcwOyR_C4_Ai_PhCLtk6DRpPNmQckeO15RiwsgjPiJB5D4Wd5k3BoLncRa8CS88rujduALsKDNlLejhhcVj09aIqAL1RjB-Qf_at6Vh02t4JQ8SBxtHy0ZbhFBZzqBjgSmvTntSE=> 

 

Funding Triggit

 

Facebook retargeting company Triggit locked in a $6 million debt facility, with North Atlantic Capital joining Spark Capital and Foundry Group as investors. The new money comes just six months after a $7.4 million raise. From the press release: "70% of Triggit's business is now international, heavily driven by Latin America and Asia. Prior to the launch of Facebook Exchange, only 16% of Triggit's business was non-US." BlueKai Stamp of Approval

 

BlueKai is launching a new data validation methodology that will focus on ensuring the accuracy of third-party data. The three-part method includes consensus testing and assigning attributes for data that is matched well. "We feel that the single-expert methodology is a flawed approach. There is far too much data across the digital landscape for one data provider or company to be the unchecked arbiter," said Pieter De Temmerman, SVP of Exchange and Global Business at BlueKai. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001pUNkJiybayQZzqb8Pk8UWIFzb_CAKuIdy5ZkHDZLzorkAUCcb5zg9udZ7eqwi6TFycEF2Ps39P14esxYkLo-ra7c0O6PkecqutxDrM6FCtZ5x8EztK0c2awrzph4GT7zgsOUSw9Ipo6SOdo4C5IJfjJeHL_98SVenEmJoqZDYZWIlNrqlk8Wjdzl_xtZazLgVUKYXDAi1PPVFRtWuxOIEIBu3BNvXmOhZ1v3YIliLd12eCWJ5q8-cA==>

Bumpy Programmatic

 

Executives from BBC Worldwide, the French ad exchange La Place Media, and Amnet weighed in on programmatic video at a recent Adap.tv event in London. Tom Bowman, VP of global strategy and sales operations at BBC Worldwide, said he "would get rid of his sales team if the yields were better via programmatic," reported ExchangeWire EMEA. La Place Media MD Fabien Magalon reportedly said his co-op's publishers were "very protective" of direct deals on online video. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001pUNkJiybayRlK3izdgHgTkXGA1p6Jf8OTFsQpbd7yW6D1jrwnQgtpuIMEKreByN_66V8P7nYltJ1TANDNiqr1VRdkTnW3NPYGocxx17wRyIRoRVwDTU_oidYk97rD-sMm5xLmOyL2wg-hwe0ud0C9XTIR3zgs9dxyAIejKjqMKG7R7OfyeInMKKwOBRL16SfJQ_57PUgaakYQBeolApiWw==> 

 

Web Video's Hurdles

 

This month's NewFront appeared to be a grand opportunity for Nielsen's Online Campaign Ratings and comScore's Validated Campaign Essentials, both which track web video in a way that is familiar to TV media buyers. The problem is, according to Adweek's Mike Shields, that web video bellwether YouTube refuses to sell according to the metrics. Secondly, other publishers have their own issues with metrics like Nielsen's OCR. "Publishers have to overdeliver significantly to deliver against OCR and they lack the tools to understand their audience," says Brian Kane, COO of Liverail, a web video tech platform. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001pUNkJiybayRYxrjuaNtIRcNEG7oQQ0NgxlVCapZU53QsB_zcv59mZ3VwIJygtKRhGr8n1VlNwGM6Swa4VSkwJGAJlsHIDGq_XS9oOVpcTLlrlHaJ_S2fBcZUySNCMPV4Eddqx8ikLzZ_g2ak3w7uBOdN2u_E7K-Bx5uihjwHQLVgFlJxQnMJqt1GNAnbHYgqXkQENDfPEnL3WJVAOetAEDXncz00gGXg3YUvdu8a7yY=> .

 

Counseling for CMOs and CIOs

 

Forrester's Sheryl Pattek makes the case for CMOs and CIOs to work more closely together, saying, "Marketing and technology have become so intertwined that technology should now be thought of as the foundation of marketing. Effective customer engagement across the ever-growing touchpoints of the digital age requires technology to support your marketing objectives." She shares several ways CMOs can do that, including understanding where the CIO is coming from, focusing on customers and their experiences first, establishing shared goals and rewards, and getting the two teams to also work together. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001pUNkJiybayQGen8ZaDW4u6XgUDcFpPDRNhHFgh2xYXLnGGxZLRJlTyuk9o01obK5TnW8QoLsdlTz8TKk0KIFFIRlyyIK0t5Y-mWuwsAs3Zx04B_1R1BZuaUCiPeBiGhZcRw-J1hMq1ZNYLHVsjfx_JaIPtOskdpeau3u5mynXYNZcImxhrg8HoyPwUBTWWjWkNU8-guuHeLZaXwqe6q2ze9FRZcs_HajpJUgPYW-8M-mVboLd6ktT0WXWDUnVWQgRS0FnM0mbKE=> .

The Trading Desk Evolution

 

Companies like Interpublic's Campbell-Mithun are cutting out what they see as middlemen - agency trading desks - and building their own digital trading operations, reports Ad Age's Alexandra Bruell. Bringing the trading desks in-house is "about an evolution from a lot of third-party data to really deep integration with first-party data," Chris Wexler, director of media strategy and interactive for Compass Point Media (Campbell-Mithun's media buying and planning group), tells Bruell. "This is the way media buying and selling is going. Offloading this capability long-term isn't the right strategy." Read the rest. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Od5ulRpxGSV3732FjxM349q_BD01ifoFwahmBNyqMbsRUyI8mWP1MkcO_VUQLGiluSvwUcfq9dwkt5BXaMBmmFoWguvWlVhfRdZHddJRuni008aaVlMO-ydUKzwNo9UgoCQ1ynTSkBkkS9CpaT7j3zwOg6GbLlyE_VCrrmsZDwn5PJtwkqLIt6QX5EqfIWNnbreWnn7aTk7NcnUndU0jMrNpF9aBRzItbJNlUnfXLJvBaVs8CUBI3Fv4s2ptMUHh>

Walmart Goes Shopping

 

Not to be left out of the acqui-hire race, @WalmartLabs (Walmart's technology arm) is ramping up its cloud and software services through two new acquisitions: OneOps and Tasty Labs. The startup OneOps comes with a Platform-as-a-Service capability that will enable the company to "significantly accelerate our PaaS and Private Cloud Infrastructure-as-a-Service strategies," writes WalmartLabs CTO Jeremy King in a blog post. Tasty Labs, which develops social media platforms, was founded by an ex-Googler, a former Mozillian, and the founder of the social bookmarking site Delicious. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Od5ulRpxGSWtJ0nErkJ4BTkIsAOMBzsrbBS44wKMBA88-6Q8JO_JQgj_0r5Mv-N3Ytk0sl1bPey8UjsNYQJ2-ebzSWrjIFWf5Whl1c7vL_NfZTLyzmZsKUPx9h14CpbaZjkcGKxmlbDaqi8c3DNva8HfpNDf0ZpJyP-aMyuUWTvV7mHJr5NlSDERx3FgJfbZZVoKJNfwqWA=>

Grounded Air

 

Google's efforts to expand its streaming music ambitions and challenge Spotify appears ready to take off, reports the NYT's Ben Sisario (Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Od5ulRpxGSWjJ0_ea79iLvVljNzR0re46RS1bUJJE2ogj9d4fkcUOdlYS5pJFiUe7FQ8Jnnq-jE_uJuS7mAiVteM4ldinc4QamEmveJsFBn_L0V62CX1qQVjuEX0lxWw9M8e9jLF28mNXpefdcYQxUQ7D3BRhtWS3inZGd-v-5790TrhdDW7HOnIt-mB47VdunZwXrStsCJM4UH3t9ajpFffQvGCiSpa_W3bJ9uZhE7vCR-L00Z-ym339KBWnShOtVBzaqx8WbQ=> ). But elsewhere Google is pulling back, namely on its nearly decade-old plan to enter the data-rich, airline reservations business. Skift's Dennis Schaal reports that Google is "discontinuing the Passenger Services System (PSS) for airlines" in order to free up resources to focus on other travel solutions for users and partners such as Google Flight Search and Hotel Finder, and ITA's QPX software suite, the company said in a statement. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Od5ulRpxGSV2yTpLYZ9devQfilC2Z7l4Ll5lZ3SwNYR8ozwYLLw90HcnWKELWxvNUQ3-QXd-dA2EfEhcHXgRhTKvRQIvCBmoxNa80pIUXLdLubWfw80ovf1CnBYlMZw9xdt_NCFy9dOfN0q_7GmkYVqePE03-LMXVTjDtuHs9AW11RW0An4XuUJLjQem-0uUYYXcR_NOrTj6xVQhNZbcdNoxdWaBUA1UAx2gTbtzuNc=> .

Extending GRPs To Mobile

 

In their TV "Upfront" presentation yesterday, Nielsen announced that it is extending its Online Campaign Ratings product to mobile apps. What's that mean, you ask: "ABC will be able to measure audience demographics and understand the reach and frequency of online campaigns across ABC content on the Web and in mobile apps." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f7YqWooFeBUbrdWk1vyIhsXWJd_zTQInAoPHsagnW29owNbvEay3RWk0ovHnUKUUZfsACFZP7rbb5w4wn0yYnkuh3gjQbdxfrcXjNBTxcYFU6rpVMBdg3tDeOCA4mLnpwYGkJkJioA0f84hvnSj7FBXy-NFOiwae9tWumuSeR6tJ5cMWEC3PZRxysnEZGY_EUu5opsZ6hUOxldf6SyHFxSG9WTAGZTwU8DPZ8w40UvyzM-PvR4J5rJozVe-5IjD1> . Marketers are looking for better ways to extend and understand their media buys across traditional and digital channels.

 

Acqui-Hire Blues

 

While Yahoo dives deeper into its acqui-hire spree, entrepreneur turned VC and prolific blogger Mark Suster exposes the dark side of acqui-hiring. Acqui-hires who are wooed for millions of dollars hurt the buyer, Suster points out, by telling loyal employees "if you want to make 'real' money-quit." As Suster argues, "So why not announce big, hairy audacious goals on recruiting the best mobile talent with sign-on bonuses and retention plans? And reward your existing top 10% of employees handsomely." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f7YqWooFeBXLp0OMcoa_4EggAT4zHwUGK_BAEEsKQhwTN-jBWsLurW7d-kuXMpdh5MwwUeHrtDNdOJ4JSWEQGReaIh-CqPG8Lr9aJ-4bNKXwLxen9Kz9jb_mJQpnxGibsfpOn6k6sf2URpplXao_63GY8SM8vsfvotTQP2hVMxV5WzL-MJzFSHBYX8pCLg5bhhNP15ur-NS21UZwv8hE2Q==> .

 

Visualization Is Coming

 

Speaking of acqui-hire, Twitter has acqui-hired a company in the data visualization space called Lucky Sort which has 3 or 4 people says Linkedin <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f7YqWooFeBV9oWgZ8_IiDmv11rRuk76qmlTqlSzfejLkC1ltMh6dpkbnopnhf49fOC9PjjWbWo37b12FXSoSC2Wm7l7GoAZPoN_MLAqB792xpHGfh0aeMOlUyges6KbmZLX50vxjU9SNzDT8QBni_fYX1c-Tkdqz> . Mo' Data Blues

 

In an age of cheap and abundant data, many brands are still using legacy approaches that stymie marketing partners. SapientNitro data/analytics guy Stewart Pratt tells AdAge's Kate Kaye the big problems are inflexible architecture, a cost-saving mentality that prevents analysis of today's huge datasets, and a need for training. He says, " Because data has historically been so costly for large companies to collect, maintain and process, they tend to limit the amount of information captured to the bare necessities and adopt analytics techniques designed for understanding small data samples." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f7YqWooFeBVv3wSF6FlmaM28YQiDvb6P1tS5R9KEUMCwcrN_7jcSQ3SfW8h0752-8xZPtuMYh5Fc1cW4vu5fwPcU8YDqSyRHmFsmeJUtS1tP-lCCmDPbjbkYWpSrer_KVMybx3oHSpO42nwZapIHqI5uedj3M2g-O1gUahgwtW8eSE6e7fH5Zpk4h68WLA38ANOdYqNwvo-7QSdZhxkTKORrsVQ46FNAy0PRr78SC2DEvlhtuurLbtydRvR5knCCC_bSr3Yb99MgvLMvyyMhlw==> 

 

Pirate Wars

 

Dan Peak's Veri-Site has been hunting online money launderers for a decade. Now the company is working with GroupM Interaction North America COO John Montgomery on developing software that generates lists of offending websites so advertisers like AT&T and Unilever never run messages on fraudulent sites, reports Adweek's Katy Bachman. "People have bought into [the idea] that it's a problem," Peak says in a Q&A. "In the next year or two, we will go a long way toward taking steps to screen and block." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f7YqWooFeBWC6JcvK_0a3bZbFq3BIODuzP8LhwE1ZJMTmkS2SxEx2rNlEl3Yk57_BqwExVzjq2LvJV4dAEmsfvxCB869G9vM0XQLPnQlvs9-7kQ29FYniXiyZolyEVopLsuhp2o6Om4PMIRlnn4GXAZDpeOHkoEjD_zBRQTVt1AnG5BC4E14HsLuTO1zrKrdaP7xS_zmyWM=> .

Cookie And Big Pubs

 

The potential demise of the third party cookie is the subject of much debate these days (see Eric Picard's recent column suggesting it's no big deal <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f7YqWooFeBUvwcfW1cAznUMthrjarfSLA7QpDdRKz3WYzWPb75tqibUd7yyBBp6GxOkWT5mw5ixEbf1q2eFyKHsi-2W2dr4hdWjz2XGnr82nqDRKlWbHkF01b5exN-ZWb5rThA4THnoag_ZBGNk0mc2uaFv8GRHGYN9enL83Dtt8do7sNH33tS39CVSgJDtrxzaAQdaHQMmBxmigomQVdw==> ). In Mediapost, Mark Zagorski, eXelate's CEO, argues that major publishers could experience some pain as well if the cookie falls into disuse. Killing the third-party cookie will not save branded publishers," he writes. "On the contrary, new, even stickier technologies, and an ad-tech industry whose focus is performance and delivery efficiency, will continue to innovate and push forward." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f7YqWooFeBVvJ7fOuSZ9LHUF3L8lZgSw6liE6J-1zeS_qPzG1U57lfVBQtUqsQCEE73WWaCeDFKwDqmst9GXV5qBZLHAGGdvHxqOYxTalWQU9eyluNHcJRiDI--m2YVfIDjdqnHw9DgIXWO4QjNVmfGSTY9YBEfKE3Dp9ETAHbtSg7AhzxOCRRqSIu0ors5Pa7fVu5gOVPrE1xDWvbZBOp4NgWPnGb3WdvIJ5VfVAC177mYU4lP4UpJUHO_HtZASEzcHS6H7ZaI5OUoa9EdkzPo0yIZV-ECx> .

 

Pandora's Way

 

Investors and the music industry are hoping that streaming internet radio player Pandora figures out a sustainable revenue model soon. Max Engel, director of Product at SpinMedia, writes in Hypebot that the company's advertising moves are going in the right direction. "Pandora already has worked to bolster its ad platform to create a display ad network that can bridge the desktop and mobile," Engel says. "The company could potentially take its ad platform and possibly take it off-network so other music sites could benefit from their deep customer insights and targeting." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f7YqWooFeBXqlJTnq8Y0cbqOlVmW3MfzTagY1jkFMOug4Y_xgtUyFIBaubOwM3FFrJOK1c_vy03ssaenWUtdRSRHzT5p7G4A_K5zBWkY9uu2MpxGq8Z1mdFsup0bnJPwDiAkHx19v51qSHOSn_dCpJUTj4ApxzIU3VgIQyhWfJ9G8Tulh9pq-ETFJYK1trEAr_eiBRddV8dt900grtUrPPKHQoXYLWZ5Pqn9pRXHJdRwC-uN2Cy_IVkSd3x3RyyT3KpzRHOZ5c_vD-brM8vj8ueb0g07yUOMrd1e74mNwmz1_pKKlk87RmU8lOe-Jz04XmD60T5ccysMWOw2vqV4wUZoixc1B7tfpVQ5nfAEmrEtlBoaH3gbb40e6tUSYLiRV5dnOlk3xq4=> .

 

Next Stop: Brazil

 

Tag management vendor Ensighten is pushing into Latin America through its new partnership with Lima Consulting Group (LCG), a digital marketing agency with offices in São Paulo, Brazil and the United States. From LCG founder and managing partner, Paul Lima's perspective, "Ensighten changes the way we work with our customers and quickens their digital marketing cadence." Programmatic 'Tipping Point'

 

Even the most optimistic acknowledge that TV dollars are beginning to make a more pronounced shift to digital. As the FT's Emily Steel notes, a wider adoption of programmatic ad sales methods is taking place, impacting the traditional face-to-face negotiations between sellers and buyers. "This year may be the tipping point where programmatic buying, which has been historically online, will make the transition to offline," said MediaLink CEO Michael Kassan. "The nature is to resist change, but I don't think they can stop it. Momentum is building. Broadcasters will have no alternative." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001DvkVT0P8ckYxeMdlXa-pldcwTf6CbVRMCG_QPDy7c-A_39UNxRqOuheUMaSs6WS-7nZOAf_J5UTF2_XpxTVbENWkZGGlvWUl6jPfxkyeuS9y-j57_5ko-ldsa0XDNya4v8fgAycEVPIjuEGiagBGuJVt6eMVx68jTxBqz-mIhaFQ3uD9d7qzbx6bdwnoXfGX> .

 

A 'Second Path' To Funding

 

Given the ubiquity of "rentable" technology (bidders, servers, data- and demand-side platforms, etc), Undertone CEO Eric Franchi says it's now easier than ever to bootstrap your way to market penetration. "For example a mobile rich media play," he blogs. "Assuming the distribution channel is in place, a company can skip right to validation via direct sales, channel partnerships or a combination of both." Surprise, surprise: This is the way Franchi says Undertone did it. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001DvkVT0P8ckZKS-F0Op9MGiHfz27qmmZ13fnZMgN32JqQV85gwNwrqh8Bh0PhMGuhxCGGS6KaP4nh34SUtYhMtO6ldC-UCvmo_f6Ii1EUcl35WH0Eu-ph4S3yznC7dDSjNIJTsz0z-ccKyhASt2LZXnK8sghrWnl9papFDDP5-8gWM6-uOren7PjiMmIeFzJy> 

 

More CRM Retargeting

 

eBay-owned display ad retargeter Fetchback is on the warpath with new set of marketing videos. "CRM targeting" is part of the mix, as product manager David Jardine explains <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001DvkVT0P8ckYvd9-oOJcHH_fsdaedFL2Qgqb5xmmp3eU949O8ymmhB0-jNCDGVFpukHq5CFd1P4UYDcolE5wv1PSf6UhrHGdv1W57hUH5M1X7BZGl7HLO6GYMq2zZIkw3UbfbWp5jjBONK-I-P8p2qA==>  how his platform differentiates itself with CRM, "We've [developed] an intensive information security process where an advertiser exports a segment of their database and encrypts it before they send it to us. And then we take that encrypted data and match it against online data so that there is no sharing of an email address between any party in the ecosystem." See the videos now <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001DvkVT0P8ckacoNKg8Jk-mDGjF88u6mBPNamkSAkpyI93mgNnSzREUBme4bMbUQ09POrp6LfI2mtJp7EJrIHUxI_6md63wEJS1kW-Y3cF6blsL9meoyw71R28WtOAr0m0kS8kWxhCshrzHer9yKdhGqadOI5eepYG> .

 

The Consultant Cometh

 

The Economist looks at changes among the big consulting players, including accounting firms (PwC, Deloitte and Ernst & Young) and pure play consultants (McKinsey, BCG and Bain). While the piece doesn't deal with the digital ad space directly, you can read between the lines here and see a bigger role for these players. From the report: "Clients are increasingly demanding specific expertise, not just raw brainpower. McKinsey and BCG, in particular, are hiring more scientists, doctors and mid-career industry types, and reducing the proportion of new MBAs in their ranks." And they're going after proprietary data. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001DvkVT0P8ckZCfwovQLo9vt6DvfnWb3Fpz62MjXf6yVTreo3bq5YoGt5O4R4zL2TKb_WFFp1k0dFyMnv-ZRzntczS0gN9l1kobFazXcToo5WZz2UV1rSbV1-WQKv6iCV4k6RLYm4QUIoX8nMMa83oz0r0htzok5xNOB9cAEaXlvNsOPgCBfzyiYANYex2YTz1grMn9Iy4lZIH10qY5VCiNUTXO8H776boKEE-o1dCN-NKMrG14LfhSg==> 

 

GM's Newest Model

 

General Motor's latest model isn't a car; it's how GM structures its technology systems. CIO Journal's Steven Rosenbush and Jeff Bennett report that the automaker is modelling its new IT system on Facebook and Google - not Ford or Hyundai. "We believe we can grow faster with stronger IT," said CIO Randy Mott. "That is why we are making investments in our own data centers and innovation centers." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001DvkVT0P8ckal-dsucHq-Gcc6x792AQViVPQaz-6Cv_39hpub4GzpUfbppii5UjRgAWwc6jCwG8VkLVZPGylmWHBK3psPjQ_eCUBwp3eaiMQUq6b5sPUb3P6gCEt6q5Ve_T4yWAugCSo1UaBuSvSQeLWH1qgyv2w55_iJ6AAxkjmFqMPdSKGXarz-XzncboLJ1vVEIO0UAYzYKlqqal4G4Z2VyKDQ8QNNyCrY9ySmlmqW7Ti2c4MZvpdndY6SzIUM> .

Brands Love Instagram (For Free)

 

AllFacebook's Justin Lafferty cites a study that shows how much major brands love Instagram these days. For example, 67% of the Interbrand 100, which include marketers such as Coca-Cola, McDonald's, and Disney, have a presence on the app, compared with 57% in February. Lafferty notes that more brands are reaching high follower counts too. But will they eventually become paying advertisers? Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001DvkVT0P8ckY5UmaL6OTPwU97f3cKybNTLLDaC0IMYdTKTxw2RUeGDPwsshTWcegXGY5NvKZx2leK2e_egfIcTGqhpS2sUx2CnLFNXPz4v9WSQCnsM_DzIq4LFGhqf5qDPCHL-Ir1yVG8Db0UPFa9jIyKQFVNjpVi9q3Z-KstkOtEohmrvZubPQ_PMHAK4im3> . You gotta start somewhere.

 

Targeting Mobile Content

 

In its latest attempt to make Google+ attractive to brands, the search giant has unveiled a new recommendations feature for mobile sites. Developers can now add code to their sites that will give users a link to related articles that have been shared or +1'd on Google+. The new feature is designed to provide readers with "the right content from your mobile website, at just the right time," claims Google on its developers blog. Read the rest. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001DvkVT0P8ckbbLwnbcEeL4NozRULm-o62eM2u4Noj0UqzP5EhNrhLmjHW-yFiSpg_hnUFfSJ1xyI6TQ5a4opNP-klA6htvTR0PSq_7rQK9H5xG7k6W-fTvpOHObcXtSS1ht4fqx_xXb8rLKru0C8xLiFPMZxBGqI8K3AEQ9zJlxE1Z6c3Ev8pvXnYYQNN4IYm>  Could the retargeting of mobile display ads somehow be next?

 

The Big Bad Marketer

 

Consumers, beware. "You are being spied on," according to China Daily's Erik Nilsson in a piece that paints marketers as data-mongers. "Web-tracking companies are logging your keystrokes, page visits - even the routes your mouse takes across pages, including where you hover and for how long. They are documenting, aggregating and selling your information to Big Data," Nilsson writes. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001DvkVT0P8ckZNVdYM_ljH-HxXhWdxIyrg5ExSC9sQVLlFmd3cDrktVDeqz3ADlUlKyMq_sLf5Ah_Xs66dNmoDFgAGChSO_XMkFLz5vXkWx7nduO5p8B-DTaMJsNAjVEK4V_P-PPtuMbT1Go8sltSb7PolnZXLKruS8K35y-L0ngkYOQjG-1ecDg==>

Ecommerce Hits $50 Billion

 

Measurement and analytics firm comScore says that digital commerce transactions crossed the $50 billion threshold in Q1. The company adds in the press release that its "new m-commerce spending estimates revealed that Apparel & Accessories was the highest grossing mobile (i.e. smartphone & tablet) product category with nearly $1 billion in Q1 sales." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001su7uBlH87EbjkqykMd9A-9_Ra7kXsCLAxSk86AdQWRkrmY7RtbXn11Tsezh-4qk9sQM4Z9H0-6ClwDk-JAkwsmgo7UHloezuoUzyutZqQOhS90FiKlWLWwnmKMdpHwI-kdw0Bc73gUy7LSIk8BUqjVCEDIZajCpPdaDKZ15MNpWV9Js2FqmZi6BBleiwqL3WkhOCFMssandlntROssAAojnYSAZwdmJ75KcVm73wKq70Xd2vuuD83bfN5jwROefGsSOXakW44yA=> . Mobile targeters take note.

 

Turner Digital Chief Walks

 

Walker Jacobs, EVP, Turner Digital Sales, is leaving the Time Warner cable network following a reorg, reports AllThingsD's Peter Kafka. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001su7uBlH87EYcbTGMlLeFtDlallXGn0RKdvhcQVL-wZTCR445M-tBDGaw9Ph_YyN_XKyON-lMO5hWGfFJ0EbRrfWEe0Ow1sVhT2LlpqsCWtqlh9CDLqWQ726rPSkY-ljNUC5J4ri50ufT_0jPo5YmCllm7SZixNqjQ5_ODLgabWzlU6wXaJ0-HDKSPuR52il7> . His position won't be directly filled. It's not clear if this signals a change in Turner's aversion to audience buying tools like ad networks and exchanges. As Jacobs told us <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001su7uBlH87EacaPGaqCruhLj-6B7ORHfl99CMfJo3jJBlMF2y0cTOJWQPNDSVnaRdcp7BJNzH5OmtAjivfhz6RYlv74RtnSt7h2Bk4GR3q62_NUAxcEdPkEICfd2ITOTUVFVr7uyMuHCZB3rhMg0AfUMj7hJaeIrClfsztbi7SfMfp7Mbzgc9_kLqIvD1n1F71gwPb6xex4dbVg_98lJrIzDIMHOWI_kQK9P39N91Qbk=>  last fall, "We believe the downside of RTB and private exchanges is that it fragments audiences."

 

Yahoo Acqui-Attributes

 

Commenting on Yahoo's acquisition spree under Marissa Mayer, PandoDaily's Erin Griffith looks at the common attributes for the acqui-hires, "All are consumer-facing. None had experienced any truly notable traction before the deal. (Astrid seems to have been the biggest with 4 million users.) Only one or two had a clear path to revenue. All were well-designed by talented teams of fewer than 10 employees. None of their products were particularly revolutionary or even unique in their categories. All of them were shut down and folded into Yahoo's offerings upon acquisition with hardly a peep of outrage from their users." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001su7uBlH87EY8gJVzKJyMdCZlDwNBLX_Goq8M3ceDo2SOOh2Dr_IyW3zch73semZ1J1DK_rzzB1TMYsRDUZLSklxYL_mFIRcol8-4FNHDhf3wnadLnD_yPbYb8c8yY_O3S1fMIbFuh3IbFhtsmvtNjQfZkxq21C53ivMsYCb1KF2QFHyScX7cJRKBR2zHEwtDfLspj9T6yFDxoAB3ygqCCQ==> 

 

Twitter's Brazil Plans

 

Twitter is obsessing about Brazil in the run up to the World Cup and 2016 Olympics. Reuters describes a recent trip by revenue boss Adam Bain, who said, ""Brazil is the largest opportunity we see in Latin America and frankly across all of the other markets."
