Real-Time Latency

 

On the MetaMarkets blog, Eric Tschetter <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001su7uBlH87EaRoZMyytf-bIdLmV-YHgMZrQ2FWmfeLYuFJG28plX4x_6DLeb7vG_mCk_ckHiX5ahIOKBoJ6xlxNBpjw_PerO3X5aFSWvRtOHsFiRQm0rL6qaJTF_bufBPIwaleLic3F4=>  shares a summary of a presentation made with Netflix at the recent Strata Conference. He ponders what "real-time" really means and begins, "I will limit our discussion of the term to its usage in the data space as it takes on different meanings in other arenas. In the data space, it is now commonly used to refer to one of two kinds of latency: query latency and data ingestion latency." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001su7uBlH87EYykf-Ec30YY2fr0G8GMWQ8z3qsYwzxFDKZyftwmjFhoTpA92BKOovpev06zzzKFNos4TiTNr4iSVo63Nvdat0TtSiXlk7Q6eWLGdSERssOFBz1Xldqf6pqcXh8UgXy2KBpEfTkYRUXJDt_nCoDjpne>  

 

Relationships Trump Fraud

 

Doug Conely of Exponential, owner of Tribal Fusion, Appsnack and Firefly Video, says that whether the buy or the sell side is to blame for online ad fraud (i.e. bots, etc.), solid relationships between buyers and sellers trump all. He continues, "...fraud is now a clear issue for programmatic buys. The industry has continuously shown an ability to raise its game to meet such challenges. If not hubris, there is at least a little bit of irony that the result of a heightened awareness on fraud will mean many platforms looking a lot more like the ad networks they have tried so hard to replace." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001su7uBlH87EYERVWAq_PoZ6zdlLVnTcuhwSnJZDmTBNt0m1SX-LtxFncXeUHs88FuLUvKo0tyCCQbmb1LdwMYgQMLFNSf5pMHLOn-LXDQSw8q3KYiYWG3eLhEL8GCL2ZarOI_bSWXGS7k2vfAjrjLW3u96MFklF7mQnRl6qa4nn498FCmNrC-qT8VrzvL25R77gE4pT2IFXkMO72qBzIiM_Is6wIcQIFGP9JZyqg8V134mvqFhbsAS7CG34qNHRruM-3elygw7mU=> . 

 

Data Is King, Content Is Queen

 

Data, not content, is king these days for publishers, Liz Schimel, Meredith's EVP & chief digital officer, tells Audience Development's TJ Raphael (she had a similar discussion <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001su7uBlH87EYBQHyBEWiitiNw_kcIUYFT1hxCvsBpmxTk_SbhlZQoAlKCa7-DjR69NVWw8Kf11m807S6KJMpQ3FoLt1aVRYpdcfTDj5WnZaG_3iQOCdxnCwcjnlCI1bWmZADTikfG2RihDa5VVpWE6eIsZqNpRhujO8sV0XgM-yA689ytB8VAQavFsjA353pi_9E73z6cMPlFKUS9sZjl9vQl3qg7EPOH>  with us at the start of the year). "Our company is about content for women," she says. "So for us content is queen, but the data we derive really underpins our strategy... Both the king and queen are extremely important, but we feel like we can't be great at our core business of creating great content and amassing scaled audiences without depth of expertise on the data side." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001su7uBlH87EZFHxyA5W7dwUs4kjchNpQJuNIBowOwVKJkMEOn_KXWg60WaNsaMtyfLVOVi1mD1t2qPu6ItSbDfX_qsXcDuaLXR5LOowUYXXwehgO4HTq3ZtU743fx6rS-F1NATk4t5-vfpn9Vd6uRQ-DzDeMt2gCIHwJww_WEcHczcpCFzp7NWg4vjiLU_VKII2A1rZ9AAQUrq5MxtSqDD8fUuKsC_6UqD2M0GmTLZRv9J2svn52qaKbh3yg-TIJerwgkx-h_dM0=> . 

 

Privacy Logout

 

Over the weekend, details emerged regarding a Bloomberg terminal privacy breech. It's not ads-related, but certainly echoes some of the worst fears: a network personally-identifies its users without their consent or knowledge. In this case, the alleged perpetrators are some journalists working for Bloomberg News, and the cookie is the terminal's login feature. Read more: The New York Times <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001su7uBlH87EbfZQq36kWUR8Mv4y0Quwgi_eXZcj5a46m3UCkCocNRGQTEhxMNsqbWX9CH_0Pdy4S3m1i6dhVBSj421asHpqtPCFYi3cfjK4q0nypEq9Rw5FyC1j53unyfCvkj66SlWZueNix4DbLXf_cJB1wU8nY0nRqJFz2jW44RNXvPPq0nMojVGIPs4J7Gkeji0t0L0C3id9m25O8BSY9aOYf9-p5p0yKoY-dpu60=> , Buzzfeed <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001su7uBlH87Eb9gr0ytiCV1WfzR-rs7LxVXUbq6mh4cgiHT6rZXG898xXy05FrfDZExQjYsDHbyUSrRGJQjdCk0wWM9hu9naIcHP65fFxsYokYkAU6idYh08YylpMEzsqMCpUHPOls2ghkKzcFLwRnbUvdiKa0fj208Tl4tsSiPhzdt8ncwtDfKghJsaryKJJwm7S0ywl6r_zoBC0RS8oX5UNQHaBHfS0W>  and Quartz <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001su7uBlH87EaJJiiONYbH_RMKJ2HVeU_QpjZ_O0qqZRvd5hD7E4NOUYDRrFI4lWUoaCXyWwc7LC1yGgUE8wi1eh1bcrb20dOfqB6cgFZwfo0fAvsIEglUGMR9b6D1Bg1PNUXwqnP_xPsJmDX1_hXmwlk7qUsecYJDvt_w7tZp9ZRh-KurJ_JsFTi2k7T68LBaGPsBuG3KG9L6s5HlNVTqjQ==> .

 

Data As A Weapon

 

Jay Fulcher, CEO of video ad platform Ooyala, has responded to the collective agency letter that appeared in Adweek, calling on AOL, Yahoo and the other NewFront participants to match the improved creative they showcased with deeper data. In a blog post, he tells the agency execs what sort of data he feels is the key weapon in marketers' video ad arsenal. "Knowing how people are watching, sharing, and discussing content is critical. But we should also be asking where they're watching, for how long, and what programs they will want to watch next," he says. Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001su7uBlH87EbzbIUyww9kT4uEubi8DkIcuHAIHcpIkeHY2LXTAailGWDwAKWzOu_bzfrMVY1D_fS7ivoH1QB0Ujs72yuo_7Vp3FnxWUxEDoHSji5fTD45L-yt85bOf2Hu9TAAc0eeH_IqorxBYsjorqNNxKWj8lth> .

Google Begins Paywall Strategy

 

Google's YouTube made it official yesterday: subscriptions are on the way for select channels. YouTube's "Team" writes on the company blog, "Starting today, we're launching a pilot program for a small group of partners that will offer paid channels on YouTube with subscription fees starting at $0.99 per month. Every channel has a 14-day free trial, and many offer discounted yearly rates." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZTYeZ44uqUNM902e6FsX1fioRGDkY-9IvsojfRUI_haBSwMsYfJDzztjiZP3RvSBSn9mjxNcgvjQ13RSUk1oVwZq361wlP6RY01KrApnzP5_dC1GF0CB_e4bsGXpLw5aqO2sjjVm5De2pCnFKfSZvKYpZoL36RyeZ7qy6ZATj8Q=> , including who the content providers are. More on The FT (subscription). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZTYeZ44uqUOhG58XHU8dc1P6TJX3-DhAad5hVWcdu1Hy8Tla7FZJUILrJjji9k0pWFYTP0_tH8uuwbKpmiRJfgnAGP_3QWbwGDpyEYSrJ2Gbqd6LYSibqWW_YKMSIrDbcsvh9wUPUT1A9hnOzqzFBNqMqQ1o9PBCA6g5eeRrmVJYn2WBHPzgmYhStxevYsx_> 

 

Facebook's Mobile Waze

 

Facebook's reported offer to buy traffic/mapping app Waze for $800 million-plus would be its second mega-mobile deal and another big play for location data. On the Inneractive blog, Hillel Fuld says the move exposes Facebook for what it is. "Facebook is a mobile advertising company and the social networking aspect is simply a mask intended to hide the entire concept on which Facebook is based. In two words, data collection. But data collection is not the goal, it is the means. The goal is to bring hyper local mobile advertising to a whole new level." Aol Sales: Certifiable

 

A day after Aol showed continued signs of a turnaround <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZTYeZ44uqUORDnoeUFTel4OZWXgKhm80YaZxXnYDe7zspLvpwKbHIUMD_L78W81arUaMgMW3zhFQ-X6x62mGYDGeGydNRB-2tdPnLcz9y68qVYRStgDL89BXifuQ1S0jKExnqn3sisLaO77k_k7up1opxb-o55szqKrXKBbPLPJp9aNlAXjJfp_NT2SnHatJ5-KQXgfKaZLdZGH5gj0apLJ4-DXJPBmTJDDRi-hc_54=>  amid the possibility of slowing growth with its third-party network revenues, the company's entire sales team will now be required to get "certified" by the Interactive Advertising Bureau's digital media sales program. Whether that will translate into higher display revenues remains to be seen. But it could be a good promotion for Aol, particularly as rival portal Yahoo attempts to jumpstart its own sales force. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZTYeZ44uqUNpSSjUZqwzSbpkcrDL2psrm6SuvGLduw9O9LB3hlm0jGcvb6hgFfKlfdx8nQqwV7-ofIn6TCmWAl9e3XFUyvx54SnN_dZbsjdMF3KiyVQ5LkydGuZEL1WWjNyi2Sdq6sldJ1svvmTixk7asPmHmwbxn_on2xfSRRPz9BeAEJIX230p3g_RzKx8dNwLJU7NiYiu2plnhk_hKuAJiBI5hlzt18UfUFVkouiValyVWx7o_pfSzN53rZM90PHGHJ1QkGcHsi8nKtqUIA==> .

 

Publisher Wants Profit

 

Say Media is laying off 10% of its 400-person workforce, according to Anthony Ha on TechCrunch. He quotes from Say CEO Matt Sanchez's message to the remaining troops: "The time is right for us to transition aggressively to continued growth with profitability. To that end, we've made a set of hard decisions aimed at right-sizing our business with a greater focus on supporting our strong content brands, growing sales and building innovative publishing and advertising products - while at the same time achieving profitability in the second half of this year." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZTYeZ44uqUOAcAEO6CRnaExjC0TnTNCeBzs0Lp4HxXRWO-rSQ8w-MNX-AfZsd_z0wrqiRW3A1b9eiFNf7OteIaJnPz8cwUzVLmbuFop1UKcjD9SyUKek-pFeD3PKY6UBBsHmry-M4HfJsgwuoMa12i4yS7l6S0ZLK9fhWL5n4E0=> 

 

Mobile Tool Fuel

 

Celtra, a company that helps clients create rich media mobile ads, has beefed up its offerings with the Interactive Advertising Bureau's Mobile Rising Stars tools. The new ad formats include pull (allows users to vertically pull a full-screen ad over the publisher content), slider (slides a banner over an ad), sticky banner (locks an ad to a designated area), filmstrip (multipanel ad) and full page flex (what it sounds like). Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZTYeZ44uqUMiiyI39PqU6UhrKSvCiVGJHYzjuLGy_JhROqZmg9JTK4_4caVOZzCQGDRSmd0CRv3YrQ2CfWumTGFAzbYB1y5fgMqz1L-bFtMdITAS6nBk0QIZhWT05VYl4XM2mKGOH8MnDmmWjJbR6yCrFkiHoZsYK-mL3LOSFgBpZEdlUpmMpMP_ZzKQHj8FK-xZKSkbqdA=> .

MEC's CookieCutter Attribution

 

WPP Group media shop MEC is introducing a digital attribution platform called CookieCutter, which the GroupM unit promises will "distill cookies into meaningful, results-driven insights and information," Theresa LaMontagne, MEC's head of analytics and insight, tells Mediapost's Steve McClellan. This moves attribution in-house and out of the hands of third-party vendors. It sounds like a good cost-cutting measure (pun sort of intended). But can the agency provide the kind of granularity for marketers that has lately come from somewhere else? Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZTYeZ44uqUOVrh5KGXC1LfRNoA87h2sqKkg9fgfHq6J1hk6x6e6L-1-dFdT7DzEfW_4yTj0H_0Q2Cqfdn0e4g5KV6AoF-cvoOTh7dC9uvqWlbykKOLn0RsaAFscveMixiymSoO8F2z5c2AvP5KNTiOuCO7Np2LLr0h54GbFfh2lBd20nRUDDldgAFMwybLkUXVksqIaP_LjWFTc1pcHLNoHOsAxtbQHIR1pbgGB8G6JsDr4UoNWK4wude6Kn239OcqzDPS2VwKk=> .

 

Need NewFront Data

 

A bunch of digital agency execs are calling on Aol, Yahoo, YouTube and other digital sellers to do better with their upfronts. Among the takeaways: give us data. In a letter published by Adweek they write, "Answer this question and you'll have lots of folks like us leaning in and listening: What are the bridge-metrics that paint a portrait of a single piece of content or programming within the broader, non-linear Web of viewing and engagement?" Marin Reports

 

Marin Software reported its first, public-company quarterly financials yesterday. On the earnings call, Marin said it is seeing "acceleration" in biz in Europe. Spend under management is also showing "double-digit growth," meaning at the very least that digital continues to grow. Read the transcript <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001poSWmkvID5nk55-EiGgmSLzCsLEGcQXW0uKGJ7I-FPPh9_uXI-Ig6C1Hzd2AjQpS3MFQ-e7E7EvOTviRgG3CUQylUA4PKcYqf_gXYa4B_S3K3rTqc4h-LKZsQjkju3sUmCux3QjAUseql9P_nrkY0iPe093fEstcdcbgvhFj3tHOYLF1ggABfQaYJFdVzEfyDZ-EZRwu6kgRhuWci2KQx3-YiVUNbb9b1D9ycvsgVc4=> . From the release, the profit and loss showed "net revenues of $17.2 million, up 32% year-over-year" in Q1 of 2013 for the SEM platform company; the company had a net loss of $10.5 million in the quarter, too. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001poSWmkvID5nK4oSRhhUjPRqSJxDDhRk9DIbU17utZptRa8Xe_ettucfUK5vcOschkoobP9o18jb-nh0bKfHmq-_EjPi4K2QLWIYiN_kq5EK884ku7eL6qZ66ZZujoYRuJLoAjn7n-05KYmunTIxemMCvqyp1Km81uivpywZ5WeYY5RzZHAa0yNyDZZ7BNIPRwp5KLk5FO9hsNEekHy5qOo6bTxvKAu8WXpo6aOiUnSVPtcjczfpOxAyVdT039oeP>  Also: "During the first quarter, 542 active advertisers utilized the Marin platform, compared to 436 during the first quarter of 2012. The Company defines active advertisers as an advertiser from whom the Company recognized revenues in excess of $2,000 in at least one month during the quarter." Marin's market cap was $438 million <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001poSWmkvID5kjWSk-auC8rJ3CAONhyRQXj4MPj3jr5cRjqH5M88dxH4Tx6xlloE-ilZ0tuLxG78eoQZ_Zkthj0jHFLGeD4j9J5-xz0vBVUIrQvRTL5IV71ENlnwXnLftC1OgBxUUNUyyVxC4E4kZK0DiT-rcDiLU0>  as of yesterday.

 

Millennial To Launch Exchange

 

Mobile ad bellwether Millennial Media said on its Q1 earnings call yesterday that it's ready to move more deeply into programmatic. It also said it was opening up its "internal" exchange to others through APIs. In a release, CEO Paul Palmieri commented on the quarter, "We delivered a major new release of our SDKs, we closed on our acquisition in the programmatic mobile space (Metaresolver <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001poSWmkvID5kUfcjf3JgC9VkBoS2SXmWF2KAyHBXPgnzV6ZLf-QzMunaLdIQNAPfxCc0svxfu6bH3ZDhnkG9veLT2iwHAIR9f_dQp11FCOkWTTzLfw_a0NbUhyg6H8wzvZFP3HsrA7846pbC9QL2CaWaLBJxRxZ7Jwynce8rhQu_1x_ktQT1fp682T0swr0id4ZIXc0MaeIwvMgRGljf1Hp_LjDw5l4PA> ), and we delivered financial performance..." MiIlennial made $49.4 million in Q1 of 2013, an increase of about $17 million from the same period in 2012. For the full year, the mobile ad network expects $270-280 million in revenue and $17 million or so in profit. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001poSWmkvID5mXt2SMgU83qM4OuE9fB7au0SPItDwbUNn4d4S9ZvoygzIshM57L1Sla-tl2mF3rBCnONxoO-D-RWdJTpooAuD-GqomKVnmSYcmKRJ_7r_kIhUvLP8dPgY6ssjv2OqPDOCpEn1LJvO5-Cuux3iS-s2szFetP7ZOKtRozae5fPAQ4Ay7DX-THSwOEaY388n5e1CkSw9TCTLgUJjpiFl7wEsl-4E7kBDaAVQRYj0PieRCxA==> . And, read the transcript of the call. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001poSWmkvID5mgRi0GHSHodRofbzCb0ONf-w5LnG1RNYWJMVAlK0avt-gqKJSQ6nanOPwSKAVo9_MjerIFJ5Y_rLAijT8dhrFarffWNjFHfyTy-8bz5nvzotQWyYYsofOTMFgGF7dPUwIGCuHSlCTd57FWXV5H4Yn0Tz8Thw8v_2zJvTbZtmGYzD-4ItJvpom1n3YQs84PQBzU1U3oABsjdYubOKoH6chBmx38vha0h8_EZYOiIl7RPg==> 

 

Data's Second Party

 

Lotame's data management platform offering has expanded to allow publishers to "syndicate" their data and create revenue-generating, second-party data relationships. The release talks a bit about how it works: "It gives the data owner full control over all aspects of the exchange process from what can or cannot be shared to the duration of time data can be accessed." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001poSWmkvID5liRQ0Ly8udmrcNJvKbREbakpmvS8WtJhHnSJTxzo-6zAbiim77amRk5tXY6QxgUMyrpXP6qfr5A7NuMYARdqjzpFW7qlPyzMlIpZ7S0s6j7V_JaXGuYvbwHniMcgGpKEqzRiP8PSIxt_PTNQTW_RdqMLqlzkw7Mz0=> 

 

DSPs In The Middle East

 

As a sign that digital advertising is making inroads into the Middle East, Adzouk, a Dubai-based ad network, has launched a demand-side platform with Google, reports GulfNews.com's Manoj Nair. The Adzouk DSP will provide advertisers with the ability to capture data, Jamie Atherton, commercial director at AdZouk, tells Nair: "There's a huge amount of data that can be pulled from RTB buys, but without the technology behind it the buyer is losing out. Our tie-up with Google gives us this technology." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001poSWmkvID5m3iYYtDevJ6pASUfaMJLten8C9xgooF9duHMUXKRIRWiVp6mW1ShkSd8VKdR6L7wOnyUqXAPOYtDKdGJ554kSTmnl6O6ZJcblARsw-pnDaaVmutm21ULBCrT9dheuZKhoO4pRuRMz8EkcFhub6OoVsjCkcF8q6wF9AuHnqv-9bzNCT5VIvqRml4Uq4aFyYdR8QTkY53ZRob1LIMjM7GKiF> 

 

News Feed Engagement

 

New test results from Nanigans confirm what advertisers have already suspected: Ads shown on Facebook's News Feed get more play than their right-rail counterparts. "Compared to FBX ads run in Facebook's easily overlooked right-hand side, FBX ads run in the desktop News Feed saw 48.4% lower cost-per-click, 197.3% higher return on investment and 17 times higher clickthrough rates," reports Adweek's Tim Peterson. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001poSWmkvID5mRA8ulEapoJEL_6BwvM8Vdugnn_fW9-TxJjOXOf5uZMSgWngWsDx64q5CnPV9MIxdMO4T89Mp1mA-VxoNW_cJV_uPHoxZmSD_TB5mlglRkl31Eluje2ZYaMaB25j1aL0U54QD74QhAx8BnmVlOubatDtGQJsYO1xGvFBJp789F6dN57WY4sF_gVaSBXe5yURwpfJ5V-8dIYLDSZVxZGWT8>

Research And Its Discontents

 

So many white papers are vendor promotions masquerading as research. Yieldbot CEO Jonathan Mendez tells Digiday's Jack Marshall that he holds comScore's five-year-old Whither the Click <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001poSWmkvID5nKCIT468VuPjTIVpwKcwa8l4B0-3_3d6hzI6IMj2afswscvgZciXoh3co55fQxO9LoIQzm59LaNo8Ulbza0-2vnZyKFkV4XdfRXo-334-e7SwjlaZ3TiKwwubeSaqvdrvt1GVClB7dA_X9m4eTDk55b1cyzxOp_xtGrtOigdrVW3gnqGYLWv-E542JSNHnoeAE9rB9E7rcGw==>  study as particularly egregious. "It got so much press through the years and was supposed to foretell a move of brand dollars to the Web," says Mendez, a longtime defender of the click. "And brands have moved into social, which is pay-per-click. Oops." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001poSWmkvID5mbal5PWoAnTTrdBxvZ-EWMv4LhIexhZyVjDQg1HFKnMzGDahBUX-KOnNdiZZ-A8v_D6ZwB5O2QyqN9DiGo0ZmQOMoYrXqop6YYTIJ2l4Zm1bNmA66TOfHe043682M4HfEM6t34u4ptOAi8Zq23dChosClpplkoXVVwefqoG4v6VQ==> .

Less Data Collection

 

Major publishers are reigning in data collection, according to Krux's annual cross-industry study on the topic. After a major leap in direct collection in 2012, the practice is now on the downswing, a trend Krux chalks up to more caution on the part of content owners. But "leakage" is a worsening problem according to the report: "Data collection per page is down, but the number of collectors and the relative percentage of collection outside of the website's control continues to rise." Also, there are more third parties engaged in data collection than ever. Download the report  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-2duFZi5j0G0axUdRp32TYzX3fhHeWmiUzA4srS6eScPd3KIQ_t7enHB02ZCQcV9PrcI0N9PWkGgIPk81fIhrbwFUeJkXgZR8E2AFed10tXsM87gQTr89fjeoWpd7L0edtcy9JSCsZZGUMKCcfb45RDM5MySEJ2XL2hzt3zJuSk=> (pay with some PII). Read WSJ's story. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-2duFZi5j0GlexvPozeAJ3Ijm5Sz12XMWIlrtHq9-ADoXaSi99LW7-N5lPj7hltJzeMY5AuYVEqrJdVpy1Dr8mBPZMdZfhJenFmFfHcSDXvjZ2k426cNWOIudQ4wnrtV_j1GglfgEFJvDt4Q_WqALoq-bUQ1-2lyHphjL9R7xXc7uvGJjYWCAaiomRPyd_CO> 

 

IPOs and Video Ads

 

Startups that let advertisers add web commercials to video clips are nipping at Google's heels, reports Bloomberg's Ari Levy. Tremor Video, YuMe and Adap.tv are expected to issue initial public offerings this year. The offerings, Levy writes, "are poised to bolster returns for venture investors, who have poured more than $230 million combined into the three companies over the past seven years, wagering that web-video promotions will become as popular as online text and banner ads." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-2duFZi5j0F8k3-ZDmLLX73TKfyrXH_Gul4218A9XNMveMitIusx3WoYxJbGnLfNIFgyqXvC75CWqf3VJacdOrHwQRuiquC4oav5O35Jhg1G6teU0jQxnarItpwzDeUtQ6ajvcnSolNrhWG3lLYphODYcS8b7J1mJsbjknQPmzoMbAibDj3qB1hM4jF6hsTbMygaPdtU3OfcxwrVOzlYsgeta4uqFZJJvkYGZTipzuU=> .

 

More Dynamic FBX

 

A Triggit blog post raves about the possibilities of more News Feed inventory for FBX buyers (AdExchanger story <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-2duFZi5j0EYsrznuOQDpin5vXI2Hn8QaTMEBw1NzgRS8HSOwla3Ga9cobvoAUaZWPQwyb33nlISvEmUleIgnPTs7JoPY-LhQbhIoGUsWbbA9g9FCCf_Wlvqw3m2j_fyO2ohlh6BZI5MznOTyA7C35Xp71Pfts31UNmPz4vRR_FlHfQfqlA4p0kE4Tq_8VfjK3Woucjc265Oq6iUqw8_LxqXqybSRB0kNA7O5SpHPoQ=> ), in particular when it comes to more creative personalization. A Slap On The Wrist

 

Ten data broker companies were caught in a sting operation by the Federal Trade Commission after agreeing to sell consumer information to undercover FTC staff members. The staff members posed as individuals seeking information about consumers to make decisions related to their creditworthiness, eligibility for insurance, or suitability for employment. The data brokers' punishment: a letter from the FTC warning the companies that their activities could be a violation of the Fair Credit Reporting Act requirements. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-2duFZi5j0Fn6sqIbi7GNUDVJX1Or3DiSnhzB5VrEvQZUmVpzmuWCx8bmwsh3DmctrT6jRJ2k8VWly4iFKMjXvBheL0mB6wnMoGq6pTH3olC-HPRYbuaZ3VZWGYrT9jlprQtrqp_FUCNcGQQOxMICiOWbK90SHfg> .

 

Auto-Play News Feed Ads

 

The FT reports that Facebook video ads are coming to its news feed in July. A cadre of FT reporters discuss the use case with auto-play: "The new video ads will appear in a user's newsfeed with the first video starting automatically but without any sound. Users will then have the option of activating audio at which point the video will restart from the beginning." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-2duFZi5j0F3RfuMaZNMq7g0O-1nt_F_RDFBlOl0sMeOLbSUCw0zqRFJVADKGarmvUQx-hkVKzAYxvIURpxiA3wnnPrHIo1McecaVRLVwSYJj3453G7kQi0qh-EgVD10RILRIeARg_CkurrHlL-N6K_KvlI1Qk3Z7pvkcJiqrKLDDSi4tROT8cHyNbvMI54a>

Millions For Location

 

Location data aggregator and provider PlaceIQ has raised an additional $6.75 million along with the $4.2 million <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-2duFZi5j0GH3vNHjdCv8ADOimLxZ1Vngm5Wogglc5fTXcDNmiK9ExufycPxWQwsXlUs-Vbu_0CcgBifxMzSsZA_amJ09BjTxjbBn9_ziho9lezdMOtHHImhxG2-EHIkn9UsS-xmvbjEjBaUj7WLbVrLJD_A-Kq2RlDHfiyYflbjLm26NBP25g==>  it raised in December 2011. Press release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-2duFZi5j0FX2lKQ6YLyEY9wbn_zmRKocdrxCKAHpYhJ44hv_Rj0LBN5oZOuDsFrVovqyKq2K0aEbYzBkpFX89Gm-TqUHlrpsdFsU17S4E3A2h46hwi06jz8I9yKuPWjpXa2b5ZF_1inZq1PoyFPcyMYy7fgdVzbZgBgsl8vkCI=> . PlaceIQ has been ahead of the mobile ad market with its location-based targeting data offering. CEO Duncan McCall, a tireless evangelist <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-2duFZi5j0HAusjNn5nJUccJMnTShVI8oHEpSL8NPZ0C_ReP0pzeV75Y861nKEz3VfgyRqMW9uH9o7xPrhQ6zimPnooqA0HGMehp5djcpsQ8Ve2BmQi3Z829barQfr8Y4YCX9eQPtNXXAj8Bmv-9S6gPfUyvMkls> , says in the release that funds will be used toward - of course - the obligatory sales, marketing and product development. Local at-scale remains a tough nut to crack for digital - mobile or not. Ideally, programmatic spend could bring it all together, but how much longer until that happens is tough to say.

It All Starts With Transparency

 

Transparency is a prerequisite for any programmatic market, says Kevin McGowan, Nexage's Senior Director of Product Management and Client Tech Services, in a company blog post. But to even get to that starting point, everyone must know what is meant by "transparency." As McGowan tells it, "Most commonly, transparency in programmatic refers to allowing a buyer to see who the publisher is and vice versa. But it goes beyond 'point' visibility. Instead, transparency means that market participants have visibility into the financial and delivery processes that span the mobile advertising transaction, and market participants have the ability to control and enforce business rules that govern how they transact." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-2duFZi5j0HuPaLU_Kt66qHegvhBg3ILh6cGYSoef4zMCYrpcVFfA6P-t7uMD19WFdfm86K8xwknVHTrY7Ei9xyXUA9fRamcoYdWX-5bsJ3I4mXZghlHxN-tStzitfBfkaLihJ_Ys-f6CtKY9TZnLvXLtzDxFfZ5DWdtJWfqlXmL6HhWC-ncrjkbRrff2u3gw13N3JIEjIQ=> .

eBay's Back

 

eBay is back in the data game, more than two years <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oIkj45nfQrgD_fCaF9xovc5PfjQ2YBNU76lpBR6AKWEZLYNzBl4TjDRH_Q2pJ3e1PRB9fZKwf2iNpWF67OruvMkbc9SYphfDaLhwKnaqWV0D-qQ1NAOBIOtMiyeeoPVA2SMqv8UOcjykL5rGp8sqUuotCdJVkfPY>  after ending its agreements with third-party data licensing companies. Brands can now access shopper data from eBay in order to segment audiences and target ads when not on eBay, similar to a recent move <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oIkj45nfQrg_j5IMQOI5cVzceEvm1SGEZM2LYhjNwj-WwokcC5h9-BCMIIVSrENcSw72HxXq4ji0wRxj5DhAnn-sX9QvYMgawTYEwcWhySa24iYbY_nstrViy0YgObfdhyMYI1luGl5EIhwhDV0kPTzTguueTVR26RFfpOr02_gwvbBNV45_Sw==>  by Amazon. An eBay spokesperson tells AdWeek, "We've recently introduced new capabilities to deliver more relevant, highly targeted digital advertising content to buyers both on and off the eBay platform on behalf of third parties, consistent with our privacy policy." The company also recently hired Glenn Fishback, previously a Turn sales exec. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oIkj45nfQriL_0SUBFdDsNWuBQ7tnbDKQGTSUI5awTXPFrdNIvyl5-cIcGGJF1LTXzEeIZj5oNxKk3nzGMyWL9ToOB2XNgFDxuI-E-RVUFwzeLtPhGbjBIglPbwDrGtjuh3aDLDMquWKNfTtU8DKBkxttn0FtissUJ_ljaXhcvGJ2pO15sHVy2QMn6KbZvcMik4BzVlXRVxHMYYzStGqpQ==> .

 

Complexity And Economics

 

Audience Science research guru Michael Greene believes the problem in digital ads isn't too much complexity; it's "broken economics" that start with the marketer. He writes in Digiday, "For many of the biggest sources of waste in digital advertising today - from bot traffic to frequency overload - [the] advertisers are the only ones capable of enforcing rules across all publisher and inventory sources." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oIkj45nfQrji0lexVD0w54zpY_Bo_eSLKejGP995qvCAkk-2fnmEOByoZTs-bCciUHveME6i4bJQIBBmsAJj8hpKbU5vJfIRjvUB9W4R9ujXEy9Hx3vazFK5YlLK_s1Qd7LANd2ZDZddwc5CncSCr_uL2nYlBQrTaa0N51TxLuNZqbeLRdA0nQ==> .

 

Apple Owns The ID

 

Apple is putting the kibosh on third-party tools that let users recommend other apps, reports PocketGamer.biz's Keith Andrew. An app developer told PocketGamer.biz that Apple rejected his app discovery tool and was informed that apps including "filtering, bookmarking, searching, or sharing recommendations" for other apps will be rejected from the App Store. "I think they [Apple] aim to be the only provider of recommendations for apps, along with being the distributor," speculated the app developer. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oIkj45nfQriOfpzE8BSEUpHvBomvfLwFk9Q9HAAm_3nuJoSX3VY9SDTlBZVQFRv8fjsUU1rCKZ_OQtSStjqEiu0rBymWPxEmZtH0tn-FUs5h6bdkRX31dlW6MjL8Ctawgm4SBQ3JJKZyCDWmq_YWoWhvL2cacAwV_QpxrrnviNWr_Ai7V7n5GlY_Uwl2rfHH> 

 

Display Defeats SEM

 

Search Engine Land's David Rodnitzky pitted Google's AdWords against the Google Display Network; when it comes to better targeting results, it's GDN's programmatic display by a "hair." The key is using these tools in concert, as Rodnitzky concludes: "The best result for almost any campaign is to max out SEM to capture folks in the last stages of purchasing, but to also identify targeting upstream opportunities on GDN and programmatic display to fuel additional demand." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oIkj45nfQrhVNyUl5OqHibly1awQAzY5UNY13_7iFedJP6WCY7Hqf2RUelzG55j-dye0gM2kPpQuIDtFfFKcmSViygBvjV3igj9GMG0IqqtbAMRBqzvBmAiFWwaVw8IDXnnC5fGHTJCUVQ6nGoT1j3zcOyNj8bh6modWQxGej1gY9HErwQbU-tOhguZuAT6uRbnwU7XsUEpPW_YS5_d_U-sqR_F3bXnR> .

 

NewFronts: Great Parties

 

Now that the Digital NewFronts are over, will TV dollars be moved to digital as a result? That's what AdAge's Michael Learmonth wondered as he reviewed a research note from Pivotal analyst Brian Wieser, who said, "If anything, a buyer reacting to inflated network-TV pricing is more likely to shift a budget toward lower-cost cable inventory." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oIkj45nfQrjCU1GmuIsf_SNk4QQdPAe8NyKERfbqT2qTANuP4yRuUMZGoaAOaBUFpvY_O0C-8ejTUoFSStZgRLxhn9QQKj6yZzOZgIKH0u5eAhUqz-SeyVyd9tZrScPYWbZvnqhZNZKyz_EjgT_--6PaUdFbxTRfh1xHUj8UDjIcrth-QInpqH2ngWg6WYxDgBXPCKOGKnc=> .

ePrize Shopping Spree Continues

 

Less than two years since beginning its shopping spree, sweepstakes content company ePrize has acquired its fifth company, Promotions.com, which uses sponsored contests and tactics designed to promise greater "engagement" between marketers and consumers. "With all the clutter in the market, it can be overwhelming when brands seek a partner to help drive digital engagement," said Matt Wise, CEO of ePrize. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oIkj45nfQrhT1CGMm_3L3qYD-UpBThnckl0ZbTQ062zYMCPgMAOlPes68pPo4BGnasPoBZDej0IMuOtAmbBzqHujoQuEnJW1p0PoXvpPY58129ZiRq_tApk9loCY1UbatHGpsgzpmB93Lv67na7lD_aNJ3mv4T9oCK2sg7GZ-PQ1Ce6aJJz7dygHFGkM6apUP-LXwUO7lGHtVptLoOjBKWnhrLwECFpJ7GJn9E31QCj1DjtVnwzShnkbJxHywkke> .

 

Consumer Insight

 

Programmatic marketing company DataXu has published a new industry report, the Consumer Index, featuring online shopping data gleaned from its marketing platform. Sample findings include that "automotive consumers are more likely to shop for media, entertainment and health products" and "online retail buyers are more likely to eat organic foods." Read the release here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oIkj45nfQrjDHvm1OnYobynKGpvOmQagnTlQkC_47JlDl02BwMVXC9mQN6ToM6qgHtgOGDM4YSmTF7rdxU32HMIwnz3PfmmCqOEsSAyAio6gn_4Rk4PJQ2TGY3hoQx_9Zxjb9-kwQf6rqjElp7vLbShn_SAiXW9PQsfunmbQHwoU8RBTC9Yj0BNF2ofoMB-F7OcccI3NMU4vt0V0_tO02IzM-ytH9DnkWi8OXQe_HdAtuo5ndyP-k4xLnkNuNgcD>  and download the report here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oIkj45nfQrhyzuU39kxg2XcW9voGC98i4AvelnvTqGeLvcR50XFjPY5z5nleox8KYfhsJemcoiR1nFjuoiL0uSGpop8MjW4on0u407kqbZvbAwCh8WEOYASF1p5yOEqfG9rO3vsqMmcOWYxVG0C2m0kH4kHocQRjbLFMsN6H4HJUjeseFzimWuCnfAIxD2dN2kRdG42ahTE=> .

 

Social Circular

 

Remember when Gannett bought Facebook ads player Blinq Media last year <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oIkj45nfQrjFkUtsb5vYSdJSZf0ZRft_VefGfdvRvoZw1pByP7W9zQ4u8H7tr635INnD10wiRirXercXtM3_plEhCRzhk_Gh2ldnvZaa5y4G7Epg38UtRP9aEzN57J-oOnvmJojnuF08yz6WyarJQ4ZUrCF0hff3xIQJbD7qvl1YKiOed3mK48icmDLHeCEjzfQ1xViY9jV4rO5t3sHRLw==> ? Well, it looks like the two are now making beautiful music - er, social ad circulars together. Writing in his Screenwerk blog, Greg Sterling presents a Facebook case study for an office supply retailer that boosted NYC in-store sales by 3.2%. The effort combined ShopLocal's circular data with geotargeting on Facebook: "Ad creatives (product images) were changed, based on user profiles and expressed interests. Basically this online-to-offline (including mobile) Facebook campaign had sent people into the store to buy." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oIkj45nfQrgC3jOn3EfWivckuwQgeh7XK7KJCDl9OZKOV9Obj0zZFLhcxoegp6VnLwZg3wKI1ZeXuMUdpQXUE8Y_FKmmIfCkeOrJd0K309-YF0EjjNHRhP9HSmjVNklXEfcIhFPXevhWWkWcXmTu67_2bM9u2WxMOnc41K-x9v2NLTNfJK3XPOHmQo9p4SwZFThofwZ4LIvjDp8f7SRQ3h7lq4X4wbRX-D7Rlju-lMI=>

 News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>   

Here's today's AdExchanger news round-up... Want it by email?
Sign-up here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rBKsQsd5SttBqnusxCnBr5CAApoMkhCgIf5vgjEc3oICn9vP9TCbjuVLS0ahSNUOTw-N8JXog8bX95kb6BASVhN8XPkClOiCYxXVHenDw-nFZtUcffqdN9p3F7qKJwUJyRItOqcIjwI=> .

 

Cookie Stuffing

 

Business Insider's Jim Edwards covers alleged affiliate marketing fraud uncovered by the FBI that centered around the use of cookies and "harmless" publisher widgets. Edwards writes, "According to the FBI, both widgets engaged in 'cookie stuffing.' Anyone who clicked on them received a tracking cookie - a small piece of code that keeps a record of the web sites a browser has been looking at. If, at a later date, those browsers went to eBay and generated revenue, then the cookie would signal to eBay that [the affiliate marketers'] links were the cause - and eBay would owe them commission (...)." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rBKsQsd5Stul2P-2A8eMon9Nbs7tPjt8ZRl6zuctA4-NSrST1TyXsuLNlyJ4tR-6_auZ-rHDz3NapKmbxH2Job3awr3HqBBf-_WuaD6UJOeVx9mezv9QepWDWHjp-EyQyfJF5X9QYjv9UpSysfDasQxEu8iGqwKcEM1QPo8Gqa03Golmt4IoH-nFHrFMNuIU> 

 

Programmatic Spikes

 

Gawker Media's Nick Denton doesn't change his negative, publisher-centric view about programmatic media in an Instant Messaging chat with Portada Online. But, he does see one bright spot, "Real-time ad exchanges can help in monetizing traffic spikes -- something that would be useful when one of our sites has a story like the Manti Teo girlfriend hoax or the discovery of the iPhone prototype." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rBKsQsd5StvAM_M7Nm7cadNoPXinh4emMAGfD8OLGVFrAhu3pkGROabQ3sWwDGg6dyfzLOy9rMwTfE3BOyKnhWepMsKH9vN4DIgkhBKKfYMeSgDBKuho8tMuPL5qCNZPBMyxsLZXPQFQuyNTroCoNHRrrb1EfbrpuCZyJuEgTlGlandUplgfe17nE_cz9Hod_iTB8LRf760fdAiVLki_W5TLeh9uEJ_NgTmFQYWxSrw=> 

 

Gloomy DNT Tidings

 

This week's Do Not Track confab of privacy and industry advocates in Sunnyvale, CA was meant to be the last face-to-face meeting before a browser spec is finalized. But the negotiators have made little progress, despite a new industry proposal issued last week (AdExchanger story <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rBKsQsd5StvNHnj-nsxl6-DYdu2Nbfms6MLb_JYIct0eDaRpwDEf6JIiqRpQARjouUUX3cvwxy6PKfrfbXZrecjE2ep7ZkCp9YIUCUa3Qx2Pn_iNfgLakU9WwkgLmXUPApcijRNjejJcClk_kCzADSiYjCmin6h0wxZpZXDXjkQYBc65zquRm_Shww3Q1VBTfsiWxtiS78h4hMo33Pd94-rtnO_wTmJVL0eAh6zFk1U=> ). The New York Times reports, "Some consumer advocates and technologists [object] to a number of prescriptive clauses in the proposal that could limit the way browsers present Do Not Track preferences to their users. A few advocates even suggested that the two sides are so far apart that the negotiations might as well be terminated." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rBKsQsd5Stvn35QlPO-palF6aFkJyr9SLGwhcU-yWkm06mGa9aDEki-Zf8UaVdOh-_tPqjFtyaMRVbTM6aGzGBInR-QI5TxSb6g4TJgbR7a0udF5UtyxjMCCPBvv3pAl5cQu6UWG5ORE8RegWZ3YwsQ6skC7JMrGApJLt0LjxifJNP5IZwKp2W0xEHp73GvbjnrIyFE9Yhng6za2nTmvP0fgZWaR5ti0> 

 

Local Pipes To Facebook

 

Yext is taking its local listings infrastructure, which pulses with local data, to Facebook. Bloomberg's Sarah Frier covers it: "Facebook (...) is adding Yext data after rolling out its Graph Search feature in January. Graph Search makes it easier for users to find friends, restaurants and interests based on social connections. By letting businesses use Yext to update their Facebook pages, the site will help ensure that information is more complete and up-to-date, Yext CEO Howard Lerman said." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rBKsQsd5SttrAWeZHTU-546ilwgKEJoO1Z_8J-2QrMGjJSAKNQ6A98T_Av_0mbWdB4X7GbTFY4yztqlYlC-uXX4UzMkT-xXvfcECcFD0aF92TyeqxanEdotXlP5f7o4YK0bjqsWGhCaRv-iYrVAFHSN9hZC49jVqo4LAYL4Rk1eb6YrcJT5p7jJsML9s6fkTbjaGsjGLVsRdfApOfXgKWrgJ_W1eIvHY>  There is a programmatic local solution in there somewhere.

 

Retargeters... On Your Mark!

 

The New York Times looks at some of the challenges around the launch of a new, U.S.-based gambling website: "At issue is whether the company can verify that the site's users are over 21 and in Nevada, using identification and geolocation software, among other tools. Visitors to Nevada can register to play before arriving in the state." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rBKsQsd5StsAtErNOJDVN5QMhtl66WkQL0zzZWmhhqRSNdNg9l0fDJsaOnNubNUhpkHLJT_byLV6qQ4vzikkJSZU_p3spbjA7BI6t9SmjXFlT9SVU50eQEnpee36CjUrNbb5wYB7aShNWFrXpk0W-80elytaRgIR324Nn_TcFOTnFgdXTaOez49YJeJ3PTlyd11VVfrMwDdFjL8i26o_JA==>  Legal, gambling online in the United States would be a big ad biz by creating a whole new audience segment (U.S. gamblers) to chase in exchanges.

"We believe the push-back on near-term Marketing Solutions revenue is what disappointed relative to most expectations. Last quarter there was a noticeable uptick in enthusiasm for an emerging mobile ad strategy." Programmatic FAQs

 

On his company's blog, Qasim Saifee, SVP of OpenX's Monetization Platform, provides an FAQ for publishers looking at the sometimes confusing world of programmatic ad sales. On bidding for ad positions in FBX, Triggit claims, "Facebook Exchange ads perform well in any position; unlike AdWords, winning the top spot isn't necessary to see great performance." Insta-Branding

 

As Facebook's mobile advertising dollars soar, it's time to get to back to work on building up revenue generation at its photo app Instagram. Last December, the app had to walk back <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SIOOb6x51A3W7gafBvAjPmAJG5GB_LStNFS-v1QatklwioOhF6oPQGOSJO9I9IdrzGfN1Gz74vkfKLHw1nOeiQpmP-SwBeXRnJOwrZki1CkSi57NwZhEKFY0ktznd72VTHgr-aeTnpIpkRNFfPNIbpKi58huOEldnhIxAGA0gwxlK9LTJ1voFg==>  plans suggesting the possible use of member photos in ads, but it appears that Instagram's new "Photos of You feature" will give marketers a new way to highlight their images. "As a business or brand, Photos of You gives you a new way to curate and share the photos that best showcase your brand as documented by your biggest fans," reads the statement on Instagram's blog. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SIOOb6x51A1Jkif5usK9GBmIZu_KRUKLroUR1OPHqLabtVZm5PdgVre71vnnOStXBMCgMWwhEQ4UhK29WYL9-7qlaSybxdMTBfzOutqkUVA5Op1kVIX8AEdcl-48whFw4kLS0olcVEzXVBoAmwg32o3gufX_OlxXfJKkFoY3QKogjFXmMAcjdGEhj7b8g_znjTfDX51Xm7g6c7wk7zVXIleioebL8uzG> .

 

Aol Ventures' Brown Goes Solo

 

Aol Ventures co-founder Mike Brown, Jr. is striking out on his own with another independent VC firm dubbed Bowery Capital, reports Fortune's Dan Primack. The fund already has $33 million in capital commitments at its debut. "Bowery data suggests that just 5% of enterprise technology spend - both internal and external - was allocated to "next-generation" solutions in 2011, but that the figure will rise to 16% by 2016 and 25% by 2020," Primack writes, citing companies like Jive Software taking market share from Salesforce.com, or Splunk vs. comScore. As for Aol Ventures, its next steps are unclear. Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SIOOb6x51A3HFXIT9nmfBOjuFAHwq1O8Wox6_XMKgUIhnpegizWU9BP0IdzI2u2NQL70XXOJs6_xfpQmwGavl8Ap9pWtT2FwPnT5u16CyVG0ufeeS9us3v9wlviCRWhLVUO1BDX8QSqrjiDu6I2FKdruyE8vX49qsj-kCBrqnaHNgiTC53pUeQ==> .

 

Digitas' YouTube Stars

 

Digitas, which founded the NewFront content and ad showcase six years ago, had some announcements of its own at its Thursday event. The Publicis interactive shop is working with Outrigger Media to find YouTube stars before they become famous. The Emerging Talent Tracker, as it's known, will track data across 50,000 "professional" YouTube channels, along with gathering engagement stats for more than 25 million videos on the site. The Tracker will "help Digitas and their clients find and engage content producers on a very granular level," says Outrigger CEO Mike Henry. In turn, it will help advertisers figure out on whom to best place pre-rolls. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SIOOb6x51A2SCodCm-qPzOZuVxnfyg4Jo14cvrIyz2Q8PHBoCzWxxTa7LKml5W8ilUduZkLjaQFMchfYl2h3AqsKyrCbnZxoD71sHlstXzn1vlR2i83ggeZWgDcBmTkq1XK_pOZDB-c=> .

 

Facebook Retail Ads

 

SocialWire raised $1 million for development of its social ad platform for commerce brands. The company helps online retailers generate Facebook ads from their website data - for instance, by taking any organic site action like a wish list add and turning it into a shareable moment on Facebook. Also announced today, Chief Revenue Officer Bob Buch became CEO. Buch wrote in a blog post, "The reason we chose to do a Seed Extension round instead of a larger Series A was because we wanted to prioritize more product development before we scale out our sales and operations...Our seed investors understand that technology is not built overnight. It takes at least two nights...maybe three. " More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SIOOb6x51A3PJEFZx2E9PPcW9IsO3brpFV9f7ZLsktqGaCNz1pgiKfXgTE35ur0A97dNn4ZgpSfw7BUQQ6YqqJJ-1WSFr7fizfm0aXJq5dQb5BTuGWBacu8svGJDQNTUkMghE6qEzrwpkEF6SotC8EEhwltHpr5RZlak7H-HiNjWnif0-DKkXZEgymtngvuj> 

 

Define "Premium"

 

On the Right Media Exchange blog, RMX account services exec Shoen Yang takes a on a few industry definitions such as "premium." Yang says, "Premium is any kind of variable that causes you to pay or bid higher than the 'open market,' fair-market value of an impression. Examples could include inventory on a household name publisher, a specific property that is rarely available, or original content or ad units that you can't get anywhere else." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SIOOb6x51A2VhiZedvwBIQG1ZBKXSNH6AaGiDHstasyOKKCyVKV7xnE0U0tn5FFUtFVlKOj7wJqHF-BQR0MtowNEMizwoA6rXpStBFF4kbbTqv2qMYhNAmL_m3cyJOyf>

Search Expansion

 

Agency holding company Aegis Media is acquiring nvi, a Canada-based search agency, in a play to expand its reach in search performance marketing. The plan is to add the search agency to Aegis Media's iProspect network. "Nvi is a market leader in search and digital in Canada," said Nigel Morris, CEO of Aegis Media Americas and EMEA, in a statement. "The Canadian performance market is evolving at a rapid pace and this acquisition will make us very well positioned to harness this growth." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SIOOb6x51A2jlkM2QVbHBemvqWaR9RzNTpQIfgcbWmDUWsUmHyFLV0fwSv5NiRazeKLzkFkoLG_O9pfXmSduVGSIe6R94nRQQEkGZ-evRa1lH29kpYbVjPdkA2Ud1074Sb2AWUcZ2nIHxS_vMaEoU1nPRe7I8lTbqN7BxJ6dcVN2sQmbFf6vQw==> .

Subsidizing Piracy

 

Piracy sites capture $6.8 million in wasted ad spend each month, DoubleVerify estimates in a new report. The verification vendor tracked 1,000 campaigns across 1,200 websites and found 3% of all "Network/RTB-purchased" impressions fell to the Jolly Roger. Download <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Ydr3kGw7YzhZzjOVM8Dka7mTktRoAmBsywRcOdMzDV_Q1uTyOTmpf9xaAKdUd4cW0_28l_hT2G77tNg6et5dEDFGPolaANhFaddV0CjzcRmeuzqjoit44d23WDiO0im3RHQSkuntTRaGKMpZapp-ok52sSoxX9W-QiUtxaQZ84yVBkczv0dZMum_J64JzNt3>  (pay with some PII). Copyright-infringing sites make up about a fifth of high-risk inventory, according to Integral Ad Science. More on this issue in our February report <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Ydr3kGw7YzhdFfkul2KJcxF3H-bl15MaEIDi8ViUjCFMRog8DXEvDKAK2pLOvHdTOn0DLn_WN3b1_9DSlXIkrnjbmiexQ8WxMi0KrFhvJIf3adD60FZWHJsRLZIJMWtv_IDfvxaVMjz0w_yHLS8gEfkkT-Tqobb6nO-gbZTQuk0zUkt3W7pftkCqL676UmqCp144jGqZvZhpgINDLN0rdj936s7uVQgu> .

 

Lights Out At Seevast

 

Internet marketing firm Seevast, the parent company of ad network Pulse 360, appeared to be shutting down (AdExchanger story <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Ydr3kGw7YzhePMt9wTjfpglKF_kYZMn6DOx1OUDDUj2omG7p-Bft8K3SPnHVMHyAoO0mWvQzU15cGizQAlnGj78bxxk_318Oci1kF-_vZFqESbPgQfPJJFmAgxnpMB0x-dCywgvb-tCusAuosP8DOJWzsC_9vtV3HxlA9J_kDVpd4DmUM9xLHhbVUQ8suCNFljOcwdDran0=> ). Buffalo Business First's David Bertola has more details, including the closing of Seevast's Getzville headquarters. Following customer complaints of late payments, Bertola noted, "On Monday, April 29 at around 2:30 p.m., the front doors were locked. Inside, a couple construction workers chatted at the receptionist's desk in inky shadows." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Ydr3kGw7Yzj5-5dtQYcFUJZ5xUzXbZ4R_y_lB6jlaXIFHcEd1x378r3ywrcW__5AC4bUu4f4tdx-b7haI61b-T8_ZbwOj01wLa2UPBeMCUwGFTMVGcu--5LJDfHX9-dmIJ8guucWsppII01Mtzi7FcAKhhSNkJcu3Xukl3AnG05bJMybQgWlhXKL_1NkZXEzdIZN6HXBjtIC2OX_14BBs9OHUgOYcvrD> .

 

Targeted Small Talk

 

Doug Weaver has some quick advice for sellers: keep your explanations and pitches to advertisers shorter than a tweet. "You could dismiss this as a gimmick if you like," Weaver writes on his blog, The Upstream. "But I'd suggest you table your disbelief for a minute and look at the underlying logic. Six word stories and 140 character 'pitches' force the seller to distill ideas down to their most powerful essence...We give our emails and our meetings a sharp, piercing quality; an agenda that says 'This will be worth my time.' Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Ydr3kGw7YzgyIKlVPAuK_Da92cqMlBEDWu_fMi-yfABbgG6ZA3PLAiK-cOOUDDVrRrqpkrTs2DH8dSW5oMWe3qe4yvhfmZz-2-DUGuZ8y5nxGqir6eTBVT-8MCpcV1EoOSvZvfRXnVkx--RCUH6C9g==> .

 

Sex (Data) Sells

 

On Digiday, Jack Marshall covers how adult content publishers are employing SEO tricks in order to drive traffic to and revenue for their site - even if they don't have any content directly related to the search terms. "We're not trying to be censors when it comes to the type of traffic that comes to the site or how it gets to the site," said Mitch Galbraith, COO and general manager of publisher Funny or Die. "We just want our chance to entertain people." Data companies may also benefit from the popularity of online adult content by putting trackers on certain websites for ad targeting purposes. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Ydr3kGw7YzjbkOFnN73JW9NpoE_4Si_2Z7fK4DCvHDJ7Fimy02WlSCTXcoXGuRQg-StNl2GZ1z7DuXQTwv-AnfzqoDT0JNAFgZsdezVcShT6WrzECqtKpCCGfcpl9jvJ4OzTULQPI8X0hskoIiSzCrv4I2udimCdY-W1Yn2BQD8gDxw_hSoHlw==> 

 

Programmatic Germany

 

Germany's penchant for premium advertising and high CPMs could be holding the country back from fully embracing programmatic buying. According to ExchangeWire, Philip Missler of InteractiveMedia "stressed a one-size-fits-all strategy will not work in Germany - and instead a more customised approach will be required in the current market environment." Hidden Ads

 

Botnets get all the glory when it comes to ad fraud, but there's plenty of malfeasance to go around. Consider "ad hiding," where ad traders load many ads (most of them unviewable) into a single ad slot - sometimes on premium sites - and then resell them through (what else?) RTB exchanges. Spider.io examines this in a new disclosure: "Whilst notably smaller than the botnet problem introduced last month, ad hiding does affect at least 2% of the inventory we are tracking through display ad exchanges and so it is significant. Ad hiding is an interesting type of fraud because the ad impressions are being served to real people (as opposed to bots)." More.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xu9profVVYI4WC_EkDwtVFnxQgufJyv1TGLtxW-6ik7oJSYyxSL0p7zk3uQX4EFSkWqIZHlN3m2bqcXiOeHEV4K5MjK22W4iCh85rPERanDEhMCSYGxq4l9WYssWITyhv717WI-rTx8iKtqe6CP_Dez4yWFxDLZzmOQOsFk4PduI4V515jfgjjztaiKz17lPCLx6JR-JlpgsUHnukq5D-73vdJ1q2GsRoJepkd5pHHs=> 

 

Wrangling Devices

 

WSJ surveys players in the mobile and multi-device tracking arena. Expedia, the lone brand quoted, gives Drawbridge's device technology a cautious endorsement. VP Jeff Warren says, "We have seen a direct positive relationship between spending on app downloads and someone consummating a transaction. Technologies like Drawbridge give me a bit of a prayer but it is still early days." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xu9profVVYL6AtK2yFab7CXCd1-gC7p8M4LG0WePM7JSEfBR-OxAWKUOvP9XOfp8sbKo6Y3fXnM_L8Pno1krNP_viCE3wc3aFpfg82QjLaxWFVypLMyRbSQgxlzm2zTlas3xkvEfaEPaDNR_toRJ6PACleYgHSBBwYKRJNI3SzRRDhfjEOLOatKotakczctTo1nmq8coAvYdljl3YhRHHHUyPv9whBie>  CNBC followed up on this theme yesterday with a video feature of its own with Tapad CEO Are Traasdahl. See it here. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xu9profVVYIwQEDGJVlgQ7VbQvB_paouVUZ_uir8glC5I8VGM_2fwUHnP8z19aMXmIrO94R48yfvUyvwCvgw4RQYgu5XQBMqJ48CEh--CpNpgxXstPga8J3NaxOYLTLoSDnTOWGqFQ9BjA8jqaENo0YLZZdzfOHwUTkc2nDC8a8=> 

 

War Of The SSP Releases

 

On Monday, sell-side platform (SSP) PubMatic sent out their "momentum" press release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xu9profVVYIzRcIEP0gFKQO8rHBg-gakIFmKeKdzcdMIDWLhLRGwOegKV1ppPEJbOG6Kn7CCmtiNtlJ4Lyqi6xilTco9jXt_3F84KK8n3iALofM-53kUoxEeGy5ykEjPaQ_eRD6iwvsDNpw0ecFueD2tKTPNykq-miUugmwnTasoWbn83jqkYu69T8onkDjaf8d0DV2fKiL7ODKb5geS-Fg2k7xDcU3y8_dn3wi2uT0Xb97ZjDtB4q0lWRGVrqhgsISctzwARGsholDPkwifSpUkhFuQ_QtDa5iNdQ2BVJReb4gn4qgQRrJMUe4wdeKClDzPWoWssuM=> . Yesterday, it was SSP Rubicon Project's turn. From the release: "For the six months ending March 31, 2013, Rubicon Project gained more than 200 new publishers and 100 new buyer channels that use the REVV Platform for display and mobile advertising." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xu9profVVYL-YC7wh2XWnFRNXWL559fneelTnA-krQC_HL5QGqIUvcVutN2szecEVGq9eWxRPKDJCWGEimPIJf32_9fsrj8_5Z9OPxmgdzj7kHwD2A1cfemABzDXJkVYwbhfdX9lyc9cj3c7Xa04C7xzZ55x8YS38u_bObgBb7xf_d1uvTER-iBvGjFK0xD5QYpNszOcR8wCc9nuRUiC9E5hUJvn87S8ExllMu8ijEYegh0eSedE0Q==> .

 

Will CMOs Disrupt the Future?

 

Over on All Things D, Russell Glass, CEO of B2B marketing company Bizo, talks about the revolution among CMOs to introduce more data-driven automation to reach customers: "The incentives for marketers to realize the holy grail of right message, right place and right time are clearly in place. So what's getting in the way of all this progress from happening immediately? Two big areas have slowed progress: Integration of data across multiple systems in the enterprise, and privacy." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xu9profVVYJcIvhXqiPoavW5MwQuuQp1Tcl0W1J_RGwwtUCeWGoi6s3pxxFqxPQR5O4Uy-7XYi49WeAao-9cw_kCPYQ1D7aKEsyh2_HFRoYXTdNWVn4HCxYY4POLs6lySHtpCGACSmGCAVTfmGqqe7DpF453LSGaI2PSQBjRofM6DwSLXZqoHmPcFxZsV1GzsdivC_Uju9gThWhkqSi4hr2TnBQ79HT2TYvHkEOjlhY=> .

 

'Non' To Yahoo

 

The French government has killed Yahoo's attempt to take a $200 million majority stake in the so-called "YouTube of France" video site Dailymotion, reported TechCrunch's Ingrid Lunden. The opposition occurred because "Dailymotion is considered a marquee company in France's technology industry," a source told TechCrunch. "Hence, [French Minister Arnaud] Montebourg, didn't want to let it go to the Americans." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xu9profVVYK3MB22EPUJveTJ9oxlR6Bvf8FAPayVDvqEecRc80grVOx02_-HbZTCuZTP5994qeK_Ntq0Et7GhEyfWV4HCft_ohBfFWGxQF_icMDE7Gie4bwVX-7bwU69Vuk_PDrpfeWpzdmfcl2Izz1HZjBkEVk_lQZMN6d8zQB7O4VYv5RZpr-UtiYpw117vU6s4tD4C5rDPUbA6WpQcLe92om-IuFEDkq3zA4g_fHnoe1U9bgX2DVPMBOMgD7u>

Money Grows On Skytree

 

Skytree has received funding for its promise to "disrupt" the Big Data space. The San Jose analytics company has some big-name backers behind its $18 million first round, including Scott McNealy, co-founder and former CEO of Sun Microsystems. "The best team wins," said Martin Hack, president, CEO and co-founder of Skytree. "The new financing will help us to aggressively grow our engineering and sales efforts in response to the expanding demand for our product." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xu9profVVYLSQx62-NLeWmZKZB5iKXJ4eGuXulJejMTTwdMDR5kYnM2N0B-2aloMfjV4Kdgm3-8JCGLMIMGOwSRoKP_41RNqK-QoHAMwIT59p9R9A3PsjKU-4NGfg7hZgPERgXXuBYA3ooReU13RJeSbaS-V7hfqAiaMUcvaeUJiCI2SOumviTH2GOORQ2bVueC0C-ZQLCD8TqnvzAeK9A==> .

 

Hulu Says Fewer Ads, Higher Engagement

 

Online video joint venture Hulu cited comScore figures touting the site as number one in engagement, compared to other ad-supported web outlets. That's generally thanks to the long-form viewing that Hulu affords, but the company also pointed to its decision not to feature TV-like ad loads, despite past resistance from backers like News Corp., which has attempted to persuade Hulu to double its ad load to be equal to TV stations. "Our reasonable ad load drives the highest recall and awareness for brands, which results in higher effectiveness for the video ads," said Acting CEO Andy Forssell in an official blog post. Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xu9profVVYKqLYiRRgJl5EuuQpu8XSlSyhyjdM07ufwKxsezSlALOlnIOd1bH9acVo0WwNi62cQJzVc0UJIv6WCKzwOI2wEvhRgLqaYQ0RwM9gdRmu-3gPUVbQVgbhTAmHlMwgBHD0CfEh1z8kl9ato5WRTwxJDx> .

Twitter's self-serve ad platform is now available to all users in the US. "Over the past year we've listened carefully to feedback from the thousands of businesses and individuals who've had access to the self-serve tool, and made enhancements based on their suggestions, including more targeting and reporting in the UI," writes Ravi Narasimhan, revenue product manager at Twitter, in a blog post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xu9profVVYJ3lW9rxb8QTnA1k9KTO-7vibZ7ZWdKIzDmGfrbAUO5ykvdY6V3QnTRRl1XiBi87o5pPHhRNcZftz9dpUKbjyYdDfkz3ZvMbBa9GM6z-VjkPSpjG9IjidOXTW7xilZ6xzQRGdAjs_DVl0Kq8EK2o89l-nuhqAsXAA4O2Yg2ltjYEhq-RwIUZAaJzNyAGiKVt_FL1Y0H1tunPQ==> .

 

Shazam! Yahoo's Riley Is CEO

 

Another rumor bites the dust: former Yahoo Rich Riley, who had been with the portal for 13 years before he left last June, was the subject of speculation <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xu9profVVYKqLYiRRgJl5PCRyEqmxEaFXynXujjaOAoaEuwQXuo1IZgBhfIslXzwGstbAFZQdm8Jx44e6RBh3gNdhThIkLoy4k_nRtathoXotPWAInLae23xDyuXJwX4ap1qK-f896hKgKoNwSK8quWj7GIP5k-35E5KJ0l8dfQ=>  a few weeks ago when many thought he would become the next CEO of display ad retargeting firm Criteo. Not even close. Audio discovery app Shazam has announced Riley as its new CEO. Previous chief Andrew Fisher is now executive chairman. He said, "Whilst Rich will run our business, I will now spend more time focusing on our corporate development and future strategy, including our ambitions to deliver a successful IPO for our shareholders as we look to become an increasingly important part of people's everyday lives."
